The Ministry of Railways Borrows Money from the Boxer Indemnity 17

Contract Signed Today

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways is borrowing 500,000 pounds from the Sino-British Boxer Indemnity Board to purchase materials in England to repair the Jinpu and Yuehan railways. The supply contract has been negotiated and finalized by Zhu Jiahao, Chairman of the British Boxer Indemnity Board, and Gu Mengyu, Director of the Ministry of Railways, and will be signed on the 24th. (Special telegram, 23rd)

Xu Yuanquan Arrives at Zhongxiang 18

Convenes a Meeting of Local Gentry

He Chengjun Still Remains at Yuekou

(Hankou) Xu Yuanquan arrived at Zhongxiang from Yuekou on the 23rd and immediately convened a meeting of local gentry to discuss the aftermath in detail. He will inspect Jingmen and other counties within the next few days. He Chengjun is still staying in Yuekou to supervise the departure of the local security forces, but the exact date has not yet been determined. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Military dispatch: There are no large groups of bandits along the borders of Henan, Hubei, and Anhui provinces. Xu Xiangqian has changed his plan to join forces with He and is attempting to flee north into the Tongbai area of Henan province. He is currently surrounded west of Maofan. The remnants of He and Duan's forces have mostly scattered, and central Hubei is quiet. (23rd Special Dispatch) (Hankou) Xiao Zhichu's unit, Zhang's regiment, occupied Daofeng Ridge on the evening of the 21st and repelled bandits attempting to seize Guanmen Mountain. The remaining bandits fled north under cover of night. In this battle, the commander of the puppet 12th Division was seriously wounded, and our regimental commander Zhang Hulin died heroically in action. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Hankou) Liang Guanying telegraphed Hankou, stating that on the 21st, he advanced to suppress bandits in Huangyun Temple, Tangchiban, and other areas in Qianshan County, western Anhui, and intercepted them from the south. The bandits were routed and are currently being pursued. (23rd Special Dispatch)

General Headquarters Promulgates Regulations for Investigating and Testing for Opium Addiction 19

(Hankou) General Headquarters promulgated ten articles of regulations for investigating and testing for opium addiction, stipulating that the Supervision Department of the Party and Government Council will handle matters in the three towns of Wuhan, the Civil Affairs Bureaus of Henan and Anhui provinces will handle matters in their respective provinces, and the county governments will handle matters in their respective counties. Anyone who is responsibly reported will be subject to investigation and testing. During the investigation period, they will be temporarily suspended from their duties. If they are proven not to be addicted, the original accuser will be punished with the crime they accused the other person of. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Fang Shao's Bandits Are Defeated 20

(Nanchang) Fang Shao stubbornly resisted in Chepan, Qianshan, relying on the terrain. Zhou Hunyuan, Zhao Guantao, and Wang Jinde advanced fiercely on three routes, capturing more than ten mountain peaks in succession, killing 2,000 bandits. Most of Fang's bandits hid in the deep mountains, while a small number fled to Qingsha Bay and attempted to cross the river to the north. Zhou's forces caught up with them, seizing 500 guns and over 40 loads of Fujian salt. The search is still underway. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Changsha) Wang Dongyuan telegraphed that remnants of bandits in western Jiangxi are surrendering to the Yue army stationed in Yingqian, and the Hunan border is peaceful. (23rd Special Dispatch)

He Xianzhu and Hong Wende

Decided to be Escorted Back to Xiamen from Shantou

(Shantou) Jiang Guangnai dispatched military judge Chen Junxiong with troops to Shantou to escort He Xianzhu, Hong Wende, He Jinshui, Wu Zongxian, and Huang Weiyu, five criminals. The Eastern District Pacification Headquarters telegraphed Chen Jitang for instructions, and Chen approved the escort back to Xiamen starting on the 24th. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Fuzhou) Cai Tingkai entered Longyan on the 20th and decided to recover Changting immediately. Mao Weishou sent another letter to Chen Peiyu, urging him to reorganize quickly. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Guangdong Authorities

Change Bandit Suppression Plan

(Hong Kong) The Guangdong authorities have changed their bandit suppression plan. The task of suppressing bandits in southern Jiangxi will be solely undertaken by Yu's army, and the titles of the two Jiangnan columns have been abolished. The task of suppressing bandits in the eastern district will still be undertaken by Li's army, and two more divisions led by Huang Renhuan and Huang Yanzhen will be dispatched to assist in the suppression of bandits in western Fujian. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) It has been decided that the expenses of the First Army Corps will be paid monthly starting from October. Arrears prior to October will also be paid in installments each month. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Hong Kong) Deng Zeru returned to the province from Hong Kong on the 23rd. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Grain Tax Collection Riot in Jiangdu

Seven Villagers Shot Dead

(Yangzhou) The grain tax collection riot has not subsided. Villagers are sounding gongs all night long. On the morning of the 23rd, several thousand villagers again attempted to cross the river. Hundreds of troops at Fuyun Gate blocked the boats from crossing. The city defense troops tried to dissuade them, but they refused to listen, so they opened fire, killing seven villagers and wounding six. The county party headquarters has convened a meeting of various agencies and organizations to discuss solutions. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Awards Given for National Products Exhibition

(Nanjing) The review committee for the National Products Exhibition, held to commemorate the third anniversary of the National Products Exhibition Hall, has completed the categorization and review of the exhibited national products and has awarded prizes in four grades. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Shaanxi Province Hopes for Central Government Subsidies

(Nanjing) Zeng Xiaoyuan, Secretary-General of the Xi'an Pacification Headquarters, said that bandits led by Cui Erdan and others in Shaanxi are harassing the Shangnan County area. Chairman Yang has dispatched troops to suppress them, and they have been routed and have fled into the mountains bordering Henan and Anhui. Shaanxi Province is currently facing financial difficulties and urgently hopes that the central government will restore subsidies. Yang may soon go to Wuhan to meet with Chiang to report on military and political affairs. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Ministry of Justice Will Pilot Prisoner Labor Road Construction 21

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice plans to request that each province allocate 50,000 to 60,000 yuan annually within their budgets to gradually improve old prisons. In addition, the Ministry plans to pilot prisoner labor road construction in Hunan Province first. If it is successful, it will be extended to the whole country. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Replacement of Railway Ties on the Jinpu Railway 22

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Railways has contracted with an American company to purchase 200,000 railway ties, which have already been delivered and are now being handed over to the Jinpu Railway Bureau for use in replacing ties on the line. The purchase price of the railway ties is over 400,000 yuan, which will be reimbursed from the revenue of the railway bureau. (23rd Central News Agency Dispatch)

Yunnan Provincial Government Pays Attention to the Vietnam Trade Treaty 23

(Nanjing) The Yunnan Provincial Government has telegraphed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting that it urge the French side to ratify the Vietnam Trade Treaty so that it can take effect and alleviate the suffering of overseas Chinese. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Ministry of Education Plans to Establish a Central University Education Museum 24

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Education has sent personnel to plan for the establishment of a Central University Education Museum. It is planned to use the museum to hold a National Education Achievement Exhibition in March next year, and a preparatory committee will be established soon. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Quartermaster General's Office Requests Revision of the Accounting System 25

(Nanjing) The Quartermaster General's Office believes that although the unified accounting system has been promulgated and implemented by the National Government, its format is extremely complex, impractical for expenditure agencies, and conflicts with the Audit Law. Therefore, it has submitted nine points of opinion, requesting revision. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Yanziji Rural Elementary School Suspends Classes 26

(Nanjing) The Yanziji Rural Elementary School has announced the suspension of classes on the 23rd due to financial difficulties and the inability to maintain operations. (23rd Special Dispatch)

US Naval Commander Arrives in Nanjing 27

(Nanjing) US Navy Rear Admiral William arrived in Nanjing aboard the warship USS Luzerne. He is scheduled to visit Navy Chief Chen Shaokuan on the 24th and then leave Nanjing for Shanghai. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Ma Bufang Determined to Attack Qamdo 28

(Nanjing) Wang Tingrui, the representative of Ma Bufang, commander of the newly formed 9th Division stationed in Qinghai, said that after Ma's troops recovered lost territory in Surmang, Gongsa, and Xiao, they advanced to Jyekundo Shiqu and will soon be able to join forces with Liu Wenhui's troops stationed in Dengke Dege. After the two armies join forces, they will cross the Jinsha River and attack central Tibet. The Dalai Lama's main camp is in Qamdo, and Ma is determined to attack Qamdo. However, the outbreak of the Sichuan war has given the Tibetan troops an opportunity to take advantage of the situation, which is unfortunate. Therefore, he visited He Yingqin to report on the current situation of his division, request supplies and equipment, and request the central government to resolve the Sichuan issue as soon as possible so that the issue of Kham and Tibet can be resolved more easily. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Ministry of Communications Streamlines the Telecommunications System 29

(Nanjing) In order to streamline the telecommunications system, the Ministry of Communications has ordered Zhong E, Director of the International Telegraph Office, to transfer the domestic radio affairs to the Ministry for takeover. The International Telegraph Office will be dedicated to international telecommunications affairs. All relevant documents will be transferred to Nanjing within a month. Whether the director's position will be changed has not yet been determined. (23rd Special Dispatch)

The Situation of Chen Duxiu and Others in Custody 30

(Nanjing) Chen Duxiu, Peng Shuzhi, and others, who are detained by the Military Law Department, have expressed their intention to request meetings with Gu Mengyu and Chen Gongbo to make certain statements. However, whether their request will be granted will be determined after Gu and Chen return to Nanjing. Chen, Peng, and others requested to read newspapers and communicate, but this has been rejected. However, their request to read books has been approved, and they are allowed to read the Three Principles of the People or other teachings of Sun Yat-sen. Visits from outside guests and newspaper reporters are strictly prohibited. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Nanjing) According to information from the Nanjing Office of the Taiyuan Pacification Headquarters, Yan is currently recuperating in Hebian Village and has no intention of returning to Taiyuan for the time being. Political measures in Shanxi Province are entirely the responsibility of the provincial government and various departments, but important matters are still decided by Yan. (23rd Special Dispatch)

(Taiyuan) Liu Shouchong arrived in Taiyuan on the evening of the 23rd. He passed through Hebian, met with Yan, and intends to stay in Taiyuan for a few days before heading south to return to Nanjing. (23rd Special Dispatch)

Foreign News

The Chairman of the Korean Delegation in the United States Declares 65

Koreans Are Determined to Resist Japan

Expressing Sympathy for the Northeast Righteous Army

A telegram from Washington to the National News Agency on the 22nd states that Li Xin'an (transliteration), who was elected President of the Korean Republic in 1910 and is currently the Chairman of the Korean Delegation in the United States, stated today that he has received a telegram stating that there are currently 10,000 Koreans in Manchuria fighting against Japanese troops. He also stated that the Japanese had encouraged Koreans to migrate to Manchuria to assist in their aggression. Now, Koreans mostly express sympathy for China in the Manchurian issue and are assisting the volunteer army in resisting Japan.

Taiwanese Aborigines Are on the Verge of Rebellion 66

Hatred of the Japanese Intensifies

A telegram from Taipei to the Far East News Agency on the 23rd states that recently, the aborigines in the mountains of Taiwan are on the verge of rebellion. They kill Japanese people at first sight. The situation is most dangerous in the Pingtung County area of southern Taiwan. Due to insufficient defenses by the Japanese police in the area, many people have been killed by the aborigines in recent days. Currently, the Japanese authorities in Taiwan are actively planning a suppression and intend to appoint the chief of the local police station as the commander of the suppression force, leading over 240 soldiers into the aborigines' territory on the 26th of this month to carry out the suppression.

Japanese Diplomacy Becomes Active 67

Implementing the Asian Monroe Doctrine

Seeking International Coordination on China

A telegram from Tokyo to the Dempo News Agency on the 23rd states that Foreign Minister Uchida said in the last Diet session that the Far Eastern issue can only be resolved through the friendship of China, Japan, and Manchuria, expressing the foundation of the so-called Far Eastern Monroe Doctrine. It is not limited to Far Eastern policy, and it is recognized that it is necessary to change the traditional approach to European and American policy. Therefore, he ordered Ambassador Izubuchi to the United States, Ambassador Hirota to Russia, Ambassador Obata to Germany, and other major ambassadors on the front line of diplomacy to return home to be given the fundamental direction of Uchida's diplomacy. At the same time, he specially sent Matsuoka to the League of Nations as a representative, and appointed Ambassador Arima to China. In this way, the lineup of Uchida's diplomacy has been gradually completed, and its full picture will be displayed to the world with the League of Nations General Assembly and Council as the center. The fundamental direction of Uchida's diplomacy is roughly as follows: (1) Continue to proceed with the spirit of international coordination without change, reject passivism, and strive for active explanation to dispel the suspicions and misunderstandings of other countries, but may withdraw from the League of Nations if confronted with unreasonable attitudes. (2) Aim to establish the principle of "Far Eastern affairs should be managed by the Far East itself" and cultivate this belief in other countries. (3) Assist the development of Manchukuo and promote the opportunity for other countries to recognize [Manchukuo]. (4) Expect China to establish a strong central government, and therefore will not hesitate to provide international assistance to related countries.

Japanese Plenipotentiary Representative to the League of Nations

Encounters a Big Storm at Sea 68

Matsuoka Deeply Concerned About the Difficulties of the Diplomatic Future

A telegram from Tokyo to the Far East News Agency on the 23rd states that, according to a telegram from the Tencho Maru received in Tokyo, the delegation led by Matsuoka Yosuke, the Japanese representative to the League of Nations, set sail from Tsuruga Port on that ship at 2:00 PM yesterday. Immediately upon reaching the sea, it encountered a large storm, with high waves making navigation very difficult. Matsuoka and his party were mentally exhausted and pale. Representative Matsuoka expressed his feelings about this great storm, saying that this trip is to fight for Japanese diplomacy, and it happens to coincide with this fierce storm and waves, which seems to be a sign of the many difficulties in the future of Japanese diplomacy. Therefore, it is difficult to predict the success or failure of this final diplomatic debate in Geneva with various countries.

Japanese Nationalist Groups 69

Planning to Achieve Great Unity

A telegram from Tokyo to the Far East News Agency on the 23rd states that the Bugei-kai, Kinno-ishin Domei, Seisan-to, and Shin Nippon Kokumin Domei of Japanese nationalist groups have traditionally lacked control, so they do not communicate with each other. Although they have the same ideology in name, their forms are divided and cannot unite. Recently, stimulated by the Japanese political situation, they feel that a great unity is essential, so they are actively planning to unite the above groups with the National Socialist Party as the center. Akamatsu, the main leader of the Socialist Party, has been running around in various directions these days and is very busy, seeking to achieve the goal of unity as soon as possible.

Japanese Residents in the United States Oppose Izubuchi's Return to Office 70

Because He Does Not Have Much Rapport with the American Diplomatic Community

A telegram from Tokyo to the Far East News Agency on the 23rd states that, according to a telegram from the New York correspondent of the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun received in Tokyo, Japanese residents in New York and Washington have expressed dissatisfaction since receiving the news that Ambassador Izubuchi plans to return to the United States. The reason is that Ambassador Izubuchi does not have much rapport with the US State Department in his diplomatic exchanges. If Izubuchi is sent to the United States again, it is feared that there will be no hope of restoring relations between Japan and the United States. Therefore, Japanese residents in various parts of the United States plan to telegraph their opposition to the Japanese government, saying that if it is necessary for Ambassador Izubuchi to return to office, he should wait until the Manchurian issue has been resolved to a considerable extent before sending him back.

Hoover Campaign Speech Surrounded by Communists 71

Veterans Join Demonstration Holding Flags

Chanting Slogans to Overthrow President Hoover

National Press Agency, Detroit, 22nd Dispatch: When US President Hoover arrived here today to give a speech, his special train was met by over two thousand young communists staging a demonstration. Hoover was trapped in the train for twenty-five minutes before he could leave the station and proceed to the Olympic Stadium clubhouse. The sound of the train whistle and the clatter of the wheels were drowned out by the shouts of the demonstrators. Communist youths, both male and female, mingled with veterans, crowded around the station, repeatedly attempting*

to rush into the station. Only when a large contingent of police arrived did they manage*

to persuade the demonstrators to the roadside, leaving a corridor in the middle for the President's*

car to pass. The demonstrators held large flags with white backgrounds and red characters, reading*

["Down with Hoover, he has caused fifteen million people to lose their jobs,"]*

Another large flag read, ["Down with Hoover, he burdens the people with huge debts."]*

As Hoover and his party drove past in their cars, the crowd became even more*

intoxicated and frenzied. Those standing on the side of the road shouted slogans such as ["He gives millions to the banks, but not a penny to you!"] Furthermore, one person wearing a tattered old army hat climbed to a high place and shouted wildly, ["Down with Hoover, the butcher of veterans!"] Not far from the station, countless leaflets were thrown at the cars, all containing abusive language towards Mr. Hoover. The end of the text claimed, ["We faced cannons in 1917 and 1918, so we can certainly face machine guns in 1932."] In addition, there were demands for bonus payments and loans in cash, all made by veterans. From the station to the meeting place at the Olympic Stadium, a distance of four miles, the sides of the road were lined with people. As the President's car passed, they were either silently speechless or uttered complaints, with no one offering praise. The President tried to force a smile in the car, but ultimately could not hide his feelings. The First Lady, sitting beside him, had her brows deeply furrowed and remained silent. It is said that, apart from when Woodrow Wilson toured the country in 1919 to explain the League of Nations plan and received silent receptions in some towns, no other major figure has ever suffered such an unpleasant reception. However, after the four-mile long journey came to an end, as soon as the President arrived at the entrance of the Olympic Stadium, thunderous cheers erupted, deafening the ears. He was immediately led by party leaders to the podium, where he delivered a carefully prepared and exceptionally astute speech. The twenty-two thousand men and women in the audience applauded constantly, their cheers resounding outside, a stark contrast to the cold reception along the way.

National Press Agency, Detroit, 22nd Dispatch: US President Hoover, in his speech at the Olympic Stadium here tonight, vehemently refuted the attacks of his political opponents and vigorously defended the government's policies. His speech was exceptionally astute, deeply moving all who listened. The speech was almost entirely focused on domestic issues, but also touched on the issue of disarmament, stating the government's recent policy, saying that the United States urgently wants to reduce armaments to alleviate the tax burden. The people and the government have already proposed principles hoping to achieve large-scale disarmament. The second step now must await the response of other countries. In these turbulent times, without an international general agreement on disarmament, the United States must not further reduce its defensive capabilities, and so on. Hoover, who had never directly criticized Democratic presidential candidate Roosevelt, this time broke the ice and directly attacked Mr. Roosevelt, demonstrating that the electoral competition between the two sides has reached the point of close combat. Automotive magnate Henry Ford was the first to welcome Hoover upon his arrival, and then sat next to the podium during the speech. After the President finished speaking, he personally escorted him to his special train and bid him farewell.

Havas, Washington, 22nd Dispatch: President Hoover, in a speech to the people in Charleston, West Virginia today, stated that he has instructed the Senate Finance Committee to thoroughly study the tariff issue, in order to understand whether American goods have appropriate protection after the devaluation of various countries' currencies. He also said, ["The current situation in the United States is improving, and I am fortunate to be able to tell you this."] The Chairman of the Senate Finance Committee also confirmed the President's statement regarding the study.

Reuters, St. Louis, 22nd Dispatch: Democratic presidential candidate Roosevelt, speaking here today, refuted President Hoover's claim that the American economic depression was caused by foreign influence, saying that the Wall Street crash of 1929 was the true starting point of the economic depression, and that the high tariffs proposed by the Republican Party exacerbated the situation, spreading it throughout the world.

Political Turmoil Brewing in France 72

The Core Issue is the Budget

National Press Agency, Paris, 22nd Dispatch: The French government's budget shortfall of eight billion francs has triggered disputes within the French cabinet. French newspapers all believe that the Herriot cabinet will soon face political turmoil due to financial problems. Furthermore, the Finance Committee has expressed absolute dissatisfaction. Herriot's failure in the National Assembly has become inevitable.

Greek Beauty Marries French Military Officer 73

Havas, Paris, 22nd Dispatch: Miss Déspina Diamantopoulou, the Greek beauty crowned Miss Europe in 1931, married French Lieutenant Colonel Weiller today. The groom's witnesses were the Secretary-General of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Berthelot, and the famous novelist Morand. The bride's witnesses were the Greek Ambassador to France, President of the current League of Nations Assembly, Politis, and the great French poet Valéry.

London to Convene Third Round Table Conference 74

Indian Princes Invited to Participate

Nationalist Party Representatives Excluded

Havas, London, 22nd Dispatch: Regarding the Indian question, another Round Table Conference will soon be held in London. The India Office has recently announced the list of Indian representatives for the conference. There are thirteen princely states within India, all represented by their respective Prime Ministers, with each state allowed only one representative. Among the representatives from the provinces, the most important are Aga Khan, representing several Muslim communities, and Ambedkar, a representative of the Untouchable caste. The number of representatives at this conference is no more than forty, a far cry from the ninety-six at the first conference and the one hundred and eight at the second. The India Office explains this by saying that "the Indian matter has reached the stage where committees are responsible for the work. All work must be made effective and actively promoted." Another noteworthy point is that there are no representatives from the Indian National Congress at the Round Table Conference. The reason is likely that the National Congress is promoting a non-violent resistance movement, and therefore was not invited to participate.

National Press Agency, London, 22nd Dispatch: The Indian Round Table Conference is expected to convene on November 15 in the House of Lords. This conference will be smaller in scope than the previous two, to facilitate the progress of work. The most important issues are the safeguards concerning finance, defense, and foreign affairs. Therefore, these three major powers will not be under the jurisdiction of the Federal Legislative Assembly in the future, but will remain in the hands of the Governor-General representing the British Crown. In addition, the future relationship between the Federal Legislative Assembly and the executive branch, as well as between the provinces, will also be a major issue considered at the conference, such as what falls under the jurisdiction of the Federal Legislative Assembly and what falls under the jurisdiction of the local legislative assemblies. Unresolved matters in the ethnic electoral system are not within the scope of the conference.

New Belgian Cabinet Formed 75

Merely a Transitional Nature

Hymans Remains as Foreign Minister

Havas, Brussels, 22nd Dispatch: A new cabinet has recently been formed, with Broqueville (Catholic Party) as Prime Minister and Minister of Agriculture, Hymans (Liberal Party) remaining as Foreign Minister, Bourgeois (Christian Democratic Party) as Minister of the Interior, Jaspar (Catholic Party) as Minister of Finance, Janson (Liberal Party) as Minister of Justice, and Denis (Catholic Party) as Minister of National Defense. All cabinet members have previously served in the cabinet, and Broqueville, Bourgeois, Jaspar, and Denis have all served as Prime Minister. Tonight, all newspapers praise the leaders of the new government. Le Soir of Belgium stated that Prime Minister Broqueville presided over political affairs for several years before and after the outbreak of the European War, with arduous and outstanding achievements, greatly benefiting the country. The newspaper then raised the question, ["Prime Minister Broqueville has formed a cabinet, but can it actually govern?"]. This statement represents the general impression. Broqueville recently issued a statement, and from the wording, it can be inferred that the new cabinet is merely transitional. The National Assembly will be dissolved imminently. The wording of the dissolution order will be agreed upon by the cabinet on Monday, and then signed by the King and immediately promulgated.

Roman Cabinet Reorganized to Vigorously Reform Domestic Affairs 76

Havas, Rome, 22nd Dispatch: At the beginning of his tenure, the new Prime Minister, Mussolini, vigorously reformed domestic affairs. He explained two of the plans he proposed to the press: (1) Decentralization of administrative organization; (2) A law passed by the National Assembly in 1926, stating that any party that obtains more than 40% of the total votes in an election will occupy 50% of the total seats in parliament, and the remaining seats will be distributed according to the proportion of votes obtained by other parties. Prime Minister Mussolini intends to abolish this method and will soon draft a bill to submit to the National Assembly. Public opinion generally supports the Prime Minister's intention. As for foreign policy, Prime Minister Mussolini adopts a flexible approach. Regarding the issue of concluding a non-aggression treaty with Russia, Mr. Mussolini and Foreign Minister Titulescu hold the same view, that the Romanian position created by the Kellogg-Briand Pact should not suffer any damage. Regarding the non-aggression matter, the negotiations conducted by the previous Vida Cabinet seem to be about to resume soon. The Romanian Ambassador to Poland, Gafencu, has met with Soviet Russian Foreign Commissar Litvinov several times in recent weeks and will soon come to Beijing to receive new instructions.

New German National Assembly to Open in Early November 77

National Socialist Party and Communist Party Compete for Chairmanship

Havas, Berlin, 22nd Dispatch: When the new House of Representatives, re-elected on November 6, opens, General Litzmann of the National Socialist Party will serve as temporary chairman. The National Socialist Party has included Litzmann in the party's list of recommendations, because they do not want Mrs. Zetkin of the Communist Party to be the temporary chairman again due to her seniority.

Balkan National Assembly Meeting 78

Romanian Foreign Minister Chairs and Delivers Speech

Havas, Rome, 22nd Dispatch: The third meeting of the Balkan National Assembly was opened by the new Romanian Foreign Minister Titulescu, who delivered the opening speech, the main points of which are as follows: ["Mutual trust and understanding between countries, and faith in the future, are the foundations of world peace. It is wrong to say that the absence of war is peace. Peace must be achieved through struggle, not merely through declarations. To consolidate peace, one must endure hardship and persevere. The difficulty of this endeavor is no less than any other great undertaking."]. Titulescu also said that the purpose of this meeting is to work towards the unity of the Balkan nations within the scope of the League of Nations.

Mussolini's Aggressive Speech 79

Havas, Turin, 23rd Dispatch: Italian Prime Minister Mussolini delivered an important speech here this morning, listing the domestic and foreign policies of Fascism. When mentioning the Disarmament Conference, Mussolini declared, "We have put forward practical and concrete suggestions, but some people have falsely accused us of being deceitful, which is the height of hypocrisy." He also said, "The policy advocated by Italy is a peaceful policy, but some people disapprove of Italy's continued existence, especially because the principles we represent are contrary to the principles they represent, and therefore they cannot be forgiven. But their principles are long outdated, and they have become a theoretical war with what we advocate. The result of this war has long been determined, and victory belongs to us." Mr. Mussolini also said, "Turin is a border city and has no fear of war." He then spoke about the League of Nations, saying, "The wishes expressed by the Fascist Party Congress have aroused the interest of the whole world. Some people ask whether Italy is still a member of the League of Nations. I now declare that the League of Nations is currently suffering from a serious illness, and we cannot abandon it. We will never abandon a patient on the sickbed. Other countries should also continue to cooperate with the League of Nations. The League of Nations is now too globalized. The more members that join the League of Nations, the more inefficient the League of Nations will become. The League of Nations can achieve results in European affairs, but in terms of the Far East and the Americas, the words of the League of Nations are merely empty words." Mr. Mussolini then said that the cooperation of the four major Western European powers is sufficient to bring peace to Europe and eliminate the economic crisis, but to achieve this goal, "Italy's sacred rights" must first be recognized. Mussolini predicted that the Disarmament Conference would fail, and then declared the Fascist Party's view of foreign policy, "We do not want any hegemony in Europe, especially if this hegemony allows the powerful to maintain their unjust position." He then mentioned the war debt issue, saying, "This debt should have been written off. We said this a year ago, but it is still unknown whether the United States will disregard its conclusions after the Lausanne Conference." Finally, Mussolini boasted about the achievements of the Fascist system in domestic affairs and concluded, "In the coming years, our new slogan will be to move forward, build, and fight when necessary."

A Good Doctor Can Be a Good Prime Minister 80

National Press Agency, Reval, 22nd Dispatch: Professor Konik, a highly respected figure in the Estonian medical community, was invited today to form a new cabinet to treat the country's chronic financial problems. Mr. Konik was one of the key figures in Estonia's independence and has been away from the political stage for many years. If he agrees to come out of retirement, he will form a non-partisan cabinet.

Lancashire Cotton Industry Strike Resolved 81

Havas, Manchester, 23rd Dispatch: The cotton industry strike has ended. Cotton mill employers and workers have reached an agreement in Lancashire to reduce wages by one shilling and six and a half pence per pound. Workers will resume work on Monday next week. This compromise will be implemented on October 31.

Pro-Japanese Atmosphere in Berlin Becomes Stronger 82

National Press Agency, Berlin, 22nd Dispatch: Germany recently celebrated the 70th birthday of Mr. Solf, the former ambassador to Japan. Japanese expatriates in Berlin all participated, causing a very strong pro-Japanese atmosphere to suddenly emerge in Germany. Important News

Future Record of Japan-US Naval Battle 83

(Continued 4)

The above naval ratio table shows that Britain is 5, the United States is 5.69, and Japan is 7.01. Therefore, Japan's submarine force is far superior to that of Britain and the United States, especially when accompanying the main fleet. Japan's holding volume is even more superior. The ratio of the number of ships, Japan's 8.4, is appropriate to the sum of the UK and the US, and the tonnage ratio, Japan's 7.67, is also equivalent to the sum of the UK and the US of 8.75. In total, Japan's 8.25 is equivalent to the UK and the US's 8.6. Therefore, Japan and the UK and US are mutually comparable in actual strength. However, the UK and the US were originally advanced countries in shipbuilding technology. Why is the naval strength of these two countries less than that of Japan? This is because after the European War, Japan gained more advantages from Germany than the UK and the US. As mentioned above, although the number of US submarines is more than that of Japan, the commander of the US Navy revealed that there were more shortcomings, saying, (Their design is obsolete and faulty) and (There is not the least doubt that the Submarine branch of the Japanese Navy is efficient highly trained, and form double,) which is enough to prove it. From this point of view, the capability of the main combat equipment in the naval battle is no longer a concern for Japan.

(B) Air Force Problem: The most terrifying thing about the future Pacific War is the air force. Once the war starts, it may not rely on the navy but use the air force to attack various parts of Japan. However, if US aircraft want to attack the Japanese mainland, they must have land-based air bases, and the US air bases, such as Sand Point and Los Feliz, may not be easy to fly close to Japan. Even if its aircraft technology is developed and the aircraft are numerous, it may not be able to cross the 4,000 nautical miles of the Pacific Ocean. Assuming that it is from Hawaii to Japan, it also reaches a long distance of 3,400 nautical miles. How can it directly threaten (Japan)? The air force strength of the major powers is compared as follows:

UK: The UK has about 1,800 military aircraft and about 900 civil aircraft. The country planned to expand its air force in 1930 and intends to increase its independent squadrons for national defense to 52 squadrons.

US: The United States has two rigid airships, about 1,000 naval aircraft, and 600 army aircraft. It is currently seeking a second expansion plan, with plans to add another 1,000 naval aircraft and 1,800 army aircraft, but the navy's budget has not yet been established.

Russia: Russia has two airships and 1,600 aircraft. It plans to form 220 squadrons by the end of 1933, increasing to 2,200 aircraft. About 500 of them are used in the Far East.

Italy: Italy currently has 1,900 aircraft and 500 civil aircraft.

Japan: The army has 580 standing aircraft, and recently prepared about 300 aircraft. The army authorities plan to organize the land troops into 17 teams by next year, increasing 136 aircraft and ○○ shipborne aircraft (translator's note: according to the Japanese newspaper last year, when the Japanese army occupied the Northeast airfield after the September 18 Incident, the Japanese robbed 173 aircraft. Most of these aircraft are the latest German and American models).

From the above, the air force strength is weaker than that of other countries, but there are no restrictions on the expansion of the air force during the Disarmament Conference. It is not yet possible to limit the extent to which the air forces of various countries will expand in the future. If war breaks out between Japan and the United States, in addition to destroying the joint fleet of the United Kingdom and the United States, the army will have to change its offensive and defensive strategy and turn to offensive operations, that is, using the air force and submarines to cooperate. On the one hand, it will begin to search for the enemy, and on the other hand, it will pass through the Aleutian Islands and Alaska from the Kamchatka Sea to Canada and the American continent. Once it reaches Alaska, (Japan)'s air force will have a landing airfield. At the same time, (Japan) must also defend against the enemy's air attacks. Currently, the country expects that aircraft will attack in four directions during the war:

East: The US fleet coming across the Pacific Ocean will use the weather to approach the enemy aircraft carrier and warships carrying aircraft in the Sea of Japan to bomb (Japan)'s territory, or launch aerial attacks when fighting the main fleet.

West: Flying from mainland China to attack (Japan). Because there are countless airfields in mainland China, once the war starts, the Japanese army will attack China in one direction and seek to occupy Hong Kong, the Philippines, and other places in the other direction. At this time, China will inevitably join the war. With the assistance of the United Kingdom, the United States, and other countries, China will also inevitably send aircraft to cross the sea and attack.

South: This is to combine the east and west sides to cut off the traffic between Japan and Taiwan. From the bases in the Philippines, Manila, Singapore, etc., they will attack northward.

North: If Soviet Russia strictly maintains neutrality, there is no need to worry. Otherwise, we will be in a very difficult situation.

At present, in order to defend against air attacks, the air defense authorities are trying to find a proper method. In the future, when the war starts, in order to prevent problems before they occur, we should first seek to destroy the enemy's bases. For example, for the enemy aircraft at sea, we should try our best to destroy their aircraft carriers and warships carrying aircraft. On the mainland of China, once the war breaks out, we should occupy its territory in advance, and at the same time, we should bomb the enemy's various facilities from the air, and order the expeditionary army to seize the enemy's air bases. As for Manchuria, it is not easy to launch aerial attacks on (Japan)'s facilities in Manchuria due to the terrain and distance.

In summary, what will be the outcome of the great Pacific naval battle between Japan and the UK and the US? In a word, it all depends on whether our army can destroy the joint fleet of the UK and the US. The comparison of the strengths of our fleet is similar. If Japan's operations are skillful and can defeat the main battleships and cruisers of the UK and the US, then the decisive battle in the Western Pacific can determine the fate of victory or defeat. In the battlefield of the South Pacific, if we can separate the enemy's combined fleet and attack it with surprise attack forces, we can expect victory. However, (Japan)'s main force will be divided into various places, which will inevitably disperse its strength. If it cannot be gathered in a timely and appropriate place, (Japan) will be in an unimaginable situation. (The above is translated from "On Pacific Strategy" by Tadataka Ikezaki and "Japan's War Against the World" by Tota Ishimaru).

Fierce Battles Between Government Troops and Bandits in Northern Hubei 84

He, Jia, and Wang Flee North; Xu's Bandits Encircled

Xu Yuanquan Goes to Zhongxiang to Personally Supervise the Suppression

Hankou Dispatch: The Fourth Army of the Red Bandits, formerly led by the puppet army commander Xu Xiangqian, fled to Suixian County in northern Hubei, attempting to join forces with He's bandits. In the battles of Changgangling and Caodian, they were severely attacked by the Independent 34th Brigade under Luo Qijiang and the 10th Division under Li Mo'an, suffering heavy losses. At the same time, He, Jia, and other bandits were also attacked between Jingmen and Zhongxiang. Although both sides tried hard to join forces, they ultimately found it difficult to achieve their goal due to the excessive pressure from the Nationalist army. It is now reported that Xu's bandits are entrenched in Maochifan. After being pursued by our army, they fled west to Shuanghe, which is the main route from Suixian County to Zhongxiang. Xu's bandits fled this way, presumably still wanting to contact He's bandits to increase their strength. After receiving the report, Garrison Commander Li Huang personally led his troops in close pursuit. On the evening of the 20th, they engaged the main force of the bandits in a fierce battle in the area east of Wujiaji. The two divisions under Li Mo'an and Jiang Fusheng, belonging to Garrison Commander Li, are elite troops of the Nationalist army. Important bandit nests such as Xiji and Jinjiazhai have all been captured by them. Xu's bandits fear them like tigers. Now, with the situation becoming critical, they are encouraging the bandits to fight to the death. From the evening of the 20th to the late night of the 21st, they are still engaged in bloody hand-to-hand combat. However, although the bandits are fierce, they are ultimately exhausted and have no way to replenish their weapons and ammunition. During one day and night, they suffered thousands of casualties, and their corpses were scattered everywhere. They were finally surrounded by Garrison Commander Li's troops. Other units have also joined in the joint suppression. In the shortest possible time, they should be completely eliminated. The groups under He Long, Jia Dechang, and Wang Bingnan are distributed in the areas of Yuanjiatai, Baiguoshu, Qushandian, and Liudian. They are being pursued by the 44th Division under Xiao Zhichu, with the two brigades of Yu Zhaolong and Wang Jinyong. The bandits collapse and flee into the mountains as soon as they encounter battle. According to captured bandits, the three bandit leaders, He, Jia, and Wang, were urgently pursued by the Nationalist army and each personally led a pistol team of over a hundred men to flee north. The remaining bandits are leaderless, making it easier to clear them out. It is reported that the Nationalist army is fighting with extraordinary courage. He Chengjun, in order to unify command, departed for Yuekou on the 18th to organize an administrative office. If necessary, he will go to the front to supervise the suppression. Xu Yuanquan left Yuekou for Zhongxiang on the 22nd to inspect the area and may personally go to the front line to supervise the troops, so that the remaining bandits in that area can be resolved as soon as possible. As for the bandits in eastern Hubei, there are still five or six thousand men, led by Cai Shenxi, the puppet commander of the 25th Army. They originally fled to eastern Hubei with Xu Xiangqian's group. After Xu's bandits transferred, Cai still remained in that area. This group suffered setbacks at Da Xiao Wenchong and fled to Qichun, Yingshan, and between Susong and Taihu in Anhui Province. Shangguan Yunxiang is personally supervising the suppression on the front lines. Hao Mengling and Gan Fang are leading a brigade of the 54th Division to flank them through Jinjiapu and Yangliuwan from Yingshan. It is reported that they have already completed the encirclement on the 21st. The 47th Division telegraphed from the front yesterday, reporting the details of the previous battles in great detail. Here is a record as follows: [On the 2nd of this month, the 139th Brigade and the 282nd Regiment of the 141st Brigade turned from near Jinjiapu towards Yangshuwan and Leijiadian to intercept the Red bandits fleeing east. That night and on the afternoon of the 3rd, they fought fiercely with over 10,000 bandits from the 75th Division, the Independent 5th Division, the guerrillas from Liu'an, Huoshan, and Yingshan, and the Independent Regiment, capturing over 100 guns and over 2,000 bandits. On the 4th, the 139th Brigade and the 282nd Regiment followed the bandits to Taojiahe in Taihu County. The bandits split into two groups, fleeing north and south. The 277th and 282nd Regiments pursued the bandits fleeing north, while the 278th Regiment turned south to pursue. The bandits fleeing north were pursued and scattered by the Li and Liu Regiments, capturing over 800 bandits and seizing dozens of guns. The bandits fleeing south were pursued for a day and night to Mataling and Jiangjiahe. On the morning of the 5th, they fought fiercely with 7,000 bandits with over 2,000 guns for 5 hours, capturing over 20 guns and over 200 bandits. The remaining bandits fled to Zhaojiapu in Taihu County. The regiment continued to pursue them and engaged them in a fierce battle at Zhaojiapu for 2 hours on the morning of the 6th. Kong Fanxiang, the commander of the 10th Company, led his entire company into the bandit ranks, seizing over 20 guns and capturing over 100 men. Company Commander Kong and Platoon Leader Li were seriously wounded, and over a dozen soldiers were wounded or killed. The bandits then fled towards Mitusi in Yingshan County. The 277th Regiment and the 282nd Regiment also arrived at Zhaojiapu through Matanhe and Dianqianhe in Taihu County at 3 p.m. on the 6th and sent teams to search for scattered bandits in Bailidun, also seizing over 10 guns. The group of bandits fleeing east was unable to withstand the relentless pursuit for several days and nights. Pei Changhui, the deputy division commander, led the 1st and 2nd Battalions of the 282nd Regiment back to Yingshan on the morning of the 7th to assist the local authorities in carrying out rural pacification. Brigade Commander Du led the entire brigade and the 3rd Battalion of the 282nd Regiment, responsible for pursuing and suppressing the bandits, arrived at Mitusi on the afternoon of the 7th. On the morning of the 8th, they followed the bandits to Zhangjiabang in Qichun County. The bandits then fled east to Susong. Brigade Commander Du led Regiment Commander Zhang to temporarily clear out the scattered bandits in Zhangjiabang. Regiment Commander Li led the entire regiment and the 3rd Battalion of the 282nd Regiment followed them and arrived at Changheka on the evening of the 8th, engaging the bandits in a fierce battle for 4 hours. On the afternoon of the 9th, they engaged the bandits in a fierce battle at Erlanghe Town for 3 hours, capturing over 100 guns and over 200 bandits. The bandits then fled northwest. The regiment pursued them to Zijinchong and Zijinshan and made contact on the afternoon of the 10th. Because the bandits had passed through the bandit areas of Mitusi and Zhangjiabang and gathered another 7,000 or 8,000 men with over 2,000 guns, the bandit forces became fierce again. Regiment Commander Li launched a fierce hand-to-hand combat against the bandits, and the bandits also held their ground and defended to the death. After 3 days and nights of fierce fighting, over 1,000 bandits were killed and over 20 guns were seized. We also suffered over 20 soldiers killed or wounded. On the 13th, Brigade Commander Du received a report from Regiment Commander Li and sent Regiment Commander Zhang through Shangxiaheng to Jiangjiashan to attack the bandits' flanks. On the 14th, the bandits were attacked from both sides and fled towards the Zijin River and Heshuijian. However, after our successive interceptions, the bandit forces were scattered. The brigade is still pursuing them in different directions towards Taihu. ] (October 22nd)

Zheng Jicheng Case Has Been Judged (Continued) 85

This court investigated the body of the deceased Zhang Zongchang. Face up, connected to the left zygomatic bone, the lower outer corner of the left eye has a handgun bullet entry wound, approximately 6 fen in length and 3 fen in width. It penetrates from the combined face to the right, with an exit wound approximately 3 fen in length and width. The left cheek has one handgun bullet entry wound, approximately 3 fen in length and 2.8 fen in width. It penetrates from the left neck, with an exit wound approximately 3 fen in length and width. Below the exit wound, there is another handgun bullet entry wound, approximately 3 fen in length and 2.8 fen in width. It penetrates from the combined face to the right shoulder near the spine, with an exit wound approximately 3 fen in length and width. Behind the head, near the top of the head facing up, there is one abrasion, obliquely approximately 4.5 fen in length and 2.8 fen in width, with broken skin and bleeding. The right arm has one abrasion, obliquely approximately 1 cun 8 fen in length and 3 fen in width, with broken skin and bleeding. It is determined to be death by gunshot. The body of Liu Huaizhou, face up, has one purplish-black mark on the left rib, approximately 9 fen in length and width, with high swelling around it, red skin inside, obliquely round 5 fen, firm to the touch. The epidermis was cut open with a knife, and one bullet was extracted. The right posterior rib near the spine has one handgun bullet entry wound, approximately 6 fen in length and 3 fen in width. The bullet did not penetrate. (The bullet extracted from the left rib facing up is the one that did not penetrate.) The outer side of the right knee has one abrasion, obliquely round 2 fen, with the skin removed, red. The right arm near the right wrist has one abrasion, approximately 1 cun 2 fen in length and 4.5 fen in width, with the skin removed, red. It is determined to be death by injury. Liu Qingxun, face up, has one handgun entry wound on the right arm, approximately 3 fen in length and width, penetrating from the combined face to the right arm, with an exit wound approximately 3 fen in length and width. Face up, the upper inner side of the left knee has one handgun bullet entry wound, approximately 6 fen in length and 3 fen in width, penetrating from the lower outer side of the left knee, with an exit wound approximately 3 fen in length and width. Only the skin and flesh were injured, not life-threatening. It has been examined and verified by the Chief Prosecutor of this court, and the examination report and injury report are on file. The defendant Zheng Jicheng repeatedly confessed without denial as to how he intended to take revenge, how he and the fugitive Chen Fengshan carried handguns to the Jinpu Railway Station, and how he killed Zhang Zongchang. This corresponds with the facts and is sufficient to serve as the basis for conviction. According to his confession: [On September 3rd, I went to the Charity Association and did not carry a gun. At 3 p.m., I returned home from the Charity Association. I heard people on the street saying that Zhang Zongchang had harmed Shandong in this way, and now he has come and should die here. He is leaving today, which is too easy for him. I was a little moved when I heard this. After returning home, I called for dinner after 5 p.m. I first drank a cup of medicinal wine. I thought that others still felt this way about Zhang Zongchang, and I had a feud with Zhang Zongchang for killing my father and was a revolutionary. How could I let him go? So I decided to kill him. I didn't even eat and called Shigunguan to ask if Zhang Zongchang had left. Because no one answered the phone, I thought he had gone to the station. So I took my handgun and bullets with me. Chen Fengshan also had a handgun and bullets with him. We took a car and first drove around to the entrance of Shigunguan on Weiyi Road. I saw the gate was covered and there were no cars in front. I guessed that he had undoubtedly gone to the station. Then we rushed to the Jinpu Railway Station. Before entering the station, I told Chen Fengshan that I was going to avenge my father and assassinate Zhang Zongchang. He followed me across the overpass to the second platform. He was protecting me. There were more than a dozen people seeing him off under the train. We mingled among the people seeing him off, all saying that the director was a lucky star. Zhang Zongchang saw his guests to the door of the train. I raised my gun and fired a shot at Zhang Zongchang, but it didn't fire. He said it was bad and turned around and ran into the train. I immediately chased after him and fired another shot, but it still didn't fire. I reloaded the bullet. Zhang Zongchang had already run to the east end of the train and was about to jump down when I fired another shot, but it still didn't fire. I chased him down to the second platform. Zhang Zongchang was about to go down to the third platform when I fired another shot. Zhang Zongchang was shot down. I rushed over and fired two more shots, and he died.] The defendant had already deeply considered the matter of killing someone and clearly had premeditation. Although he firmly denies that he personally shot and killed Liu Huaizhou and Liu Qingxun, according to his confession: [He (referring to Zhang Zongchang) had been a director, so I expected him to have guards. Since I was avenging my father and eliminating a scourge for Shandong, I was going to do it at the cost of my life.] This shows that the defendant had an indeterminate intention regarding the people accompanying him who were affected by the assassination of Zhang Zongchang. Furthermore, before entering the station, he informed Chen Fengshan of his plan to assassinate Zhang Zongchang, ordering him to bring a gun with him. The actions of killing Zhang Zongchang, Liu Huaizhou, and Liu Qingxun were indeed carried out jointly by Chen Fengshan and the defendant. In addition, Xia Tingfang, who witnessed the incident at the scene, testified: [Liu Huaizhou was injured first, and then Liu Qingxun and Zhang Zongchang were also injured. I saw two people (referring to the murderers), one wearing a gray long gown, and I didn't pay attention to the other one.] Patrol Captain Bi Shizhen testified: [I saw Chen Fengshan aiming the gun at Zhang Zongchang. Chen Fengshan said that he was avenging his military commander.] This is sufficient to prove that they were joint principals. They should each be responsible for the entirety of the crime. The argument that the killing was not premeditated and that the killing of Liu Huaizhou and Liu Qingxun was an unforeseeable fact is an empty excuse and should not be adopted. However, the defendant and Chen Fengshan killed three people simultaneously at the same place with a common intention. Although the result was a distinction between completed and attempted, it was a case of committing several crimes with one act. Therefore, the heavier punishment should be imposed. Furthermore, before the crime was discovered, the defendant surrendered himself to the officers and soldiers of the enforcement team stationed at the station. This has been certified by the Military Law Office of the Third Route Commander of the Punitive Expeditionary Army and is consistent with the statements of Li Fusheng, a member of the enforcement team, and Patrol Captain Bi Shizhen. The punishment for the principal crime should be reduced by one-third. Investigating the cause of the crime, it is indeed for the purpose of avenging his father, and the circumstances are still worthy of sympathy. The principal punishment should also be reduced by one-half. The two handguns and twenty-eight bullets and one bullet head used for the crime all belong to the defendant and should be confiscated.

Based on the above arguments, in addition to the co-offender Chen Fengshan's whereabouts being unknown and the trial being suspended, Zheng Jicheng's premeditated murder should be sentenced in accordance with Article 315 of the Criminal Procedure Law, Articles 42, 74, 284, Paragraph 1, Item 1, 38, Paragraph 1, 77, 87, 79, Paragraph 2, first section, 80, Paragraph 2, second section, 292, 57, Paragraph 5, 60, Item 2, 62, Paragraph 1, and 64 of the Criminal Law, with the judgment as stated in the main text.

This case was executed by Zhu Weiran, the prosecutor of this court, in court. The appellate court for this case is the Shandong High Court. The appeal period is ten days, starting from the date the judgment is served. October 19th, 21st year of the Republic of China, Shandong Jinan District Court Criminal Collegiate Panel, Acting Presiding Judge Li Hongye, (Seal), Judge Li Guixi, (Seal), Judge Zhou Peiji, (Seal)

Legislative Yuan Passes the Administrative Litigation Law 86

The Legislative Yuan passed the Administrative Litigation Law at its 207th meeting on the 22nd. The full text is as follows: (Article 1) If a person's rights are infringed upon due to an illegal disposition by a central or local government agency, and they have filed a re-appeal in accordance with the Appeal Law but are dissatisfied with the decision, or if no decision is made within 30 days of filing a re-appeal, they may file an administrative lawsuit with the Administrative Court. (Article 2) When filing an administrative lawsuit, a claim for damages may be attached. The provisions of the Civil Law shall apply to the aforementioned claim for damages, except for the procedures for administrative litigation, but the loss of profits stipulated in Article 216 is not included. (Article 3) No appeal or protest may be made against the judgment of the Administrative Court. (Article 4) The judgment of the Administrative Court shall have binding effect on all relevant government agencies with respect to the case. (Article 5) The jurisdiction of the Administrative Court to accept lawsuits shall be decided ex officio. (Article 6) In addition to the provisions of Article 32 of the Civil Procedure Law, a judge shall recuse himself and shall not perform his duties if he has one of the following circumstances: 1. The judge participated in the disposition or decision of the lawsuit in a central or local government agency; 2. The judge participated in the trial of the lawsuit in court. (Article 7) The parties to an administrative lawsuit may appoint an agent to represent them in the lawsuit. The agent shall submit a power of attorney to prove his power of attorney. (Article 8) If an administrative lawsuit is filed due to dissatisfaction with the decision of a re-appeal, it shall be filed within 60 days from the day following the date of service of the re-appeal decision. If it is filed because no decision is made on the re-appeal, it shall be filed within 60 days from the day following the expiration of the 30-day period. (Article 9) The execution of a disposition or decision by a government agency shall not be suspended due to the filing of an administrative lawsuit, unless otherwise stipulated by law. However, the Administrative Court or the government agency that made the original disposition or decision may suspend it ex officio or at the request of the plaintiff. (Article 10) An administrative lawsuit shall be filed in writing. The complaint shall contain the following items and shall be signed, sealed, or fingerprinted by the plaintiff or agent. If they cannot sign, seal, or fingerprint, they may have someone else write their name and the writer shall state the reason and sign: 1. The name, age, gender, place of origin, occupation, and residence or domicile of the plaintiff. If it is a legal person, its name, office, and the name, age, and gender of its representative; 2. If an administrative lawsuit is filed by an agent, the name, age, gender, occupation, and residence or domicile of the agent; 3. The government agency of the defendant; 4. The decision of the re-appeal and the statement of the lawsuit; 5. The grounds for the lawsuit and evidence; 6. Date. (Article 11) If the Administrative Court examines the complaint and believes that an administrative lawsuit should not be filed or violates legal procedures, it shall dismiss it with a ruling stating the reasons. However, if the complaint is only in a form that does not comply with legal requirements, it shall order it to be corrected within a specified period. (Article 12) After the Administrative Court accepts an administrative lawsuit, it shall serve a copy of the complaint and other necessary documents on the defendant within a specified period and order them to respond.

Page 8

(Article 13) The defendant's response shall be in duplicate, and the Administrative Court shall serve a copy of the response on the plaintiff. (Article 14) The Administrative Court may, if it deems necessary, order the plaintiff and defendant to make a second response in writing within a specified period. (Article 15) If the defendant's government agency does not send a litigation agent or submit a response and fails to respond even after the Administrative Court has set another period and urged them in writing, the Administrative Court may investigate the facts ex officio and make a judgment directly. (Article 16) Administrative lawsuits shall be judged based on the documents. However, the Administrative Court may, if it deems necessary or at the request of a party, designate a date and summon the parties and participants to court for oral arguments. (Article 17) When making oral arguments, the parties and participants may supplement documents, correct errors, and present new evidence. (Article 18) The Administrative Court may, if it deems necessary, summon witnesses or expert witnesses. If a witness or expert witness has the circumstances listed in Articles 290, 299, or 311 of the Civil Procedure Law, the Administrative Court shall rule on the penalties. (Article 19) The Administrative Court may designate a judge or entrust a court or other government agency to investigate evidence. (Article 20) Requests regarding administrative litigation procedures shall be decided by the Administrative Court. (Article 21) If the Administrative Court finds that the lawsuit is justified, it shall revoke or change the original disposition in a judgment. If damages are claimed in addition, it shall also make a judgment. If the Administrative Court finds that the lawsuit is unjustified, it shall dismiss it in a judgment. The same shall apply if damages are claimed in addition. (Article 22) If one of the circumstances listed in Article 461 of the Civil Procedure Law exists, a party may file a lawsuit for retrial with the Administrative Court against its judgment. (Article 23) A lawsuit for retrial shall be filed within 60 days. The aforementioned period shall be calculated from the date of service of the judgment. If the grounds for the lawsuit occurred later or were discovered later, the period shall be calculated from the date of occurrence or discovery. (Article 24) Regulations on administrative litigation fees shall be determined separately. (Article 25) The execution of the judgment of an administrative lawsuit shall be carried out by the Administrative Court by submitting it to the Judicial Yuan for submission to the National Government for instruction. (Article 26) Matters not stipulated in this law shall be governed by the Civil Procedure Law. (Article 27) The date of implementation of this law shall be determined by order.

Guangdong Provincial Bank Continues to Issue 3 Million New Fractional Currency Notes 87

To Recover Old Central Bank Notes

Guangzhou Dispatch: The Guangdong Provincial Bank previously issued 3 million yuan in provincial fractional currency notes, which are circulating in the market and are quite convenient. This 3 million yuan worth of one-yuan fractional currency notes is guaranteed by the provincial bank's preparation of 1.5 million yuan in cash, and the Finance Department's designation of two special taxes in Guangdong Province, the slaughter tax and the sugar tax, totaling over 2.92 million yuan in fractional silver. If an accident occurs and the cash is insufficient for redemption, the government will simultaneously add a paper tax to these two designated special taxes, collecting enough to cover the 1.5 million issued in new currency notes, and then stop adding the tax according to the plan. Since the issuance of the first phase of 3 million fractional currency notes, almost all of them have circulated in the market. Recently, because the Finance Department will unseal the Central Bank notes of various shops that were sealed last year starting on the 11th of this month, there are about 1.1 million yuan of redeemable Central Bank currency in this sealed amount. The Guangdong Provincial Bank is concerned that once these Central Bank notes are unsealed, a large number of Central Bank notes will suddenly flood the market for redemption, causing temporary congestion and hindering circulation. They consulted with the Finance Department and agreed to redeem all of these redeemable Central Bank notes with new fractional currency notes from the Guangdong Provincial Bank in order to regulate the situation and avoid affecting circulation. However, the 3 million new fractional currency notes issued in the first phase by the provincial bank have little left. Now, when the ten-yuan new fractional currency notes are approved to be used, the bank will also issue another 3 million new fractional currency notes. This second batch of 3 million new fractional currency notes is not limited to one-yuan or ten-yuan denominations, depending on temporary needs, in order to be used for redeeming old Central Bank notes when they are unsealed. Yesterday, the provincial bank prepared another 500,000 yuan in cash and redeemed 1 million yuan in Central Bank notes, and sent them to the Supervisory Committee for safekeeping, and received 3 million yuan in new fractional currency notes for issuance. The remaining 50% security deposit will be handled according to the first phase's plan. The Finance Department designated two special taxes in Guangdong Province, the slaughter of cattle and cattle skin tax of 1.2 million yuan in fractional silver, and the special tax on foreign paper of about 650,000 yuan in fractional silver, totaling over 1.85 million yuan, as the reserve fund for the second issuance of 3 million new fractional currency notes by the provincial bank. The Finance Department issued a public notice on the 16th. It has been found that merchants and people have been going to the provincial bank to receive these new fractional currency notes for days, and the reported amount received is over 2 million yuan, and the amount issued by the provincial bank for days has also been over 1.6 million yuan. (October 18th)

Scheduled to be Held in Henan Province

Jinan Dispatch: After the Ministry of Internal Affairs River Affairs Conference last year, the Hebei, Shandong, and Henan provinces have a joint Yellow River affairs organization. The first conference was held in Daming this spring and decided on many important cases. Now that autumn is high and the water has receded, the river is peaceful and safe, so the joint river affairs organization has scheduled a second conference to be held in Henan on the 9th and 10th of next month in order to discuss the important cases of joint river defense in the three provinces next year. The Shandong River Affairs Bureau received a letter from Chen Ruzhen, the director of the Henan River Affairs Bureau, on the 20th, asking them to send personnel to participate at that time. Based on this, the River Affairs Bureau has requested the provincial government to select a commissioner to attend. It is heard that Zhang Lianjia, the director of the River Affairs Bureau, will still go to Henan to attend. He is currently preparing proposals.

In addition, the Hebei River Affairs Bureau is scheduled to hold a river safety celebration on the 24th of this month and sent a letter to the Shandong River Affairs Bureau asking them to send personnel for guidance. Zhang Lianjia sent Pan Yifen, the chief of the engineering section of the bureau (Pan is currently traveling from Jinan to the upper reaches with Wang Yingyu, a commissioner sent by the Ministry of Internal Affairs to inspect the Yellow River), to represent them and participate in the celebration.
