Ministry of Communications Planning to Establish a Wireless Radio Station in Guiyang 139

Arrangements Completed, Electrification Expected Soon

The Ministry of Communications, due to the many mountains and ravines in Guizhou, the closed-mindedness of the people, and the inconvenience of transportation, specially ordered the International Telecommunications Bureau to establish a wireless radio station in Guiyang, the capital of the province. In the winter of last year, the former director, Mr. Lu Guixiang, planned everything. It is now learned that the wireless radio station there has been set up, and all the equipment has been successively transported for assembly, and electrification is expected soon.

Order from the Marine Administration Bureau for the Marine Engineers Association to Investigate the Nationality of Crew Members 140

To Find Ways to Settle the Unemployed

Since moving to its new address on Xinwen River, the Chinese Marine Engineers Association has been actively organizing its affairs and making every effort to provide relief measures, given the current shortage of maritime talent. Recently, the Shanghai Marine Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications ordered the association to investigate the nationality of crew members on various ships in order to thoroughly provide relief. The original text is recorded as follows: "For notification purposes, according to Instruction No. 2789 of the Ministry of Communications, in order to order the matter, the nationality of the crew members hired by the national shipping companies has never been reported to the Ministry, so it is impossible to know how many of the crew members currently used on various ships are Chinese and how many are foreign, which greatly hinders the statistics of crew members. It is necessary to investigate in detail in order to audit. In addition, the regulations on crew member certificates stipulate that those who have not obtained certificates shall not be allowed to serve as crew members. It is found that crew members in various regions often obtain certificates only after taking office, or they are rejected by shipping companies and still hire them because their salaries are lower, and continue to serve. It is necessary to strictly ban this practice, which treats navigation as a game, in order to ensure safety. As for crew members who have obtained certificates but are unemployed, this is inevitable. Given the current shortage of maritime personnel, it would be a pity to let them remain idle or change careers. A detailed investigation should be conducted in order to find ways to settle them. It is ordered that the above-mentioned items be investigated and reported separately in order to make overall arrangements and facilitate investigation. This order is hereby given. In addition to the separate investigation forms for foreign crew members, one copy of each, the association is ordered to investigate and fill out the forms in detail according to the above-mentioned items and send them to the Bureau for verification and forwarding. This notification is hereby given."

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Asks Shanghai County 141

To Investigate and Prohibit Rice Boats from Being Intercepted

The Municipal Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Shanghai County Government yesterday, stating: "Sir, on the 21st of this month, we received a letter from the Bean and Rice Trade Association stating that they had read in the economic news column of the Xinwen Bao on the 18th of this month that the source of rice in the Shanghai South Rice Market yesterday was almost zero, and it was rumored that it was caused by a certain gang of boat owners stopping rice boats in the inland river. At the same time, according to news from boatmen, the Lianyi Association of Shanghai South rice merchants, gathered by the Tongli gang, has dispatched more than 30 accomplices since the 17th of this month to intercept rice shipments at the Zhoupu Tangkou, forcibly blocking a large number of rice boats heading to Shanghai and empty boats returning from Shanghai, etc. The Lianyi Association often uses the excuse of heavy bushels to cause trouble for the Hushi hired by our association members. According to previous reports, it seems that they intend to escalate the situation in order to shift the blame. However, the food supply in this city relies entirely on the supply from rice-producing areas, and the daily demand is huge. If the above news is indeed accurate, the source will be cut off and there will be no way to continue, and panic will be seen immediately. The consequences are unimaginable. We humbly believe that our association members are bearing the aftermath of the turmoil, and at this time of financial drought, they are all indifferent to their business. Therefore, although their actions do their best to hinder, they do not have much gain or loss in the business prospects of our association members. However, it is worrying that the food in this city will cause panic and endanger public security. We ask for your attention and specially ask the Shanghai County Government to thoroughly investigate the matter. If the association does have the situation of intercepting rice boats, they should be severely arrested and punished to deter evil-doers, so that rice boats can come and go freely, and the food supply can be maintained and hidden dangers eliminated." The Lianyi Association of Shanghai South Rice Merchants, if it is indeed the case that rice boats are intercepted from entering Shanghai as reported, will affect the people's food supply to a great extent. In order to maintain the source of food in the area, it is appropriate to send a letter to your government to send personnel to investigate in detail. If the report is indeed accurate, it is intended to strictly prohibit it, so that the source of rice will not be lacking, and the public interest will be truly served.

Muslims Hosted the Press Yesterday 144

Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai Islamic Mosque Federation held a symposium at the Islamic Society to host reporters because the Shanghai Beixin Bookstore published a book called [Little Pig Bajie] and drew pictures on the cover, publicly insulting Islam. First, Chairman Ha Shaofu delivered a speech, saying that the Federation has decided to seek a fair solution through legal means and asked the press for assistance. Then Ma Tianying, Wang Qingyu, and others successively explained the general idea, saying that Beixin Bookstore refers to Pig Bajie as the ancestor of Muslims, which is the worst slander of Islam. Therefore, the various Islamic mosques in Shanghai have a federation to negotiate with Beixin according to law. Islam prohibits the consumption of pigs, wine, blood, those who die from natural causes, and ferocious birds and beasts that are not ruminants, as well as animals that may be harmful to hygiene and morality. Anyone who has studied Islam knows this. However, one or two reckless people, only for the sake of manuscript fees, or for other purposes, use the fact that Muslims do not eat pork to point to Muslims as the descendants of pigs, and then attach the Journey to the West to do their best to insult Islam. Those who understand the truth recognize that this publication is of no value, but the impact of this book cannot be ignored. This book is a children's reading material. In the pure thinking of children, the wrong concept of pigs as the ancestors of Muslims has existed since childhood, forming a psychology of contempt for Islam, leading to future disputes between Muslims and non-Muslims. Non-Muslims without permanent positions laugh at Muslims based on this kind of false statement, which is even easier to cause conflict. The author said that this article is [intentionally defaming Muslims in anti-Islamic education], but deliberately disclosed it, and said [for dissemination], which is obviously intentional insult. At this time, when the country is in urgent need and we are jointly resisting foreign aggression, how can there be such an absurd publication that can create serious civil disputes? Therefore, we have decided to file a lawsuit according to law to ban its publication and impose appropriate punishment on the author and publisher. We also ask the press to provide guidance. Then, tea and refreshments were served and the meeting adjourned.

Chen Yinsheng Assassinated 149

Received a Call from a Friend to Dine Out

Suddenly Shot Dead on the Spot by an Enemy

Chen Yinsheng, 33 years old, a native of Pudong, with the childhood name of Da Adi, lived at No. 6 Zhizhong Lane, Xixinqiao Street (also known as Baliquiao Street), French Concession. He independently opened the Jiangdong Restaurant near Xinkai River and had some savings. The furnishings in his home were magnificent and the arrangement was elegant and clean. At about 6 pm last night, Chen was tidying up trivial matters at home when he suddenly heard the telephone ringing. He picked up the receiver and listened carefully, and learned that it was his close friend Zhou Caitou who had called, inviting Chen to have dinner at the home of his friend Shen Hexun at No. 1 Shandeli, Zhaoqing Road, Fangbangqiao, French Concession. After Chen heard the phone call, he immediately dressed and left his home, and went straight to Shen's residence. However, just as Chen left his home, Chen's friend Gu Zhangsheng followed closely and asked Chen where he was going. The family replied that he had just gone to Shen Hexun's house for dinner. Gu then got up and went straight to Zhaoqing Road. However, as soon as he entered Shen's house, he was about to step upstairs when he suddenly heard four gunshots from the pavilion upstairs. Gu knew that something had happened, so he quickly retreated and ran to report to the police station. The captain immediately sent Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. They only saw Chen had fallen dead in the pavilion. Upon closer inspection, he had one bullet in his chest and one in his right wrist. When they touched him, his body was already ice-cold. Further inspection of the entire house revealed that there was no one else, only heavy wooden furniture was left. Finally, ninety rounds of pistol bullets and a magazine were confiscated. The body was then transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Branch for autopsy and reported for today's court inspection. The deceased has an elderly mother in the hall, Zhang, 61 years old, wife Ding, 30 years old, elder brother Yinfu, younger brother Miaosheng, one son and two daughters. The son's name is Baoyuan, 8 years old, the eldest daughter Baozhu, 7 years old, and the youngest daughter Baoyan is still in infancy. As for the murderers, Zhou Caitou and Shen Hexun, it is heard that both are Chen's closest old friends. Zhou and Shen had both served as detectives in the Municipal Public Security Bureau. All the insurance policies were found by Chen on their behalf. The deceased was stout and obese and usually liked to wear Western clothes. Yesterday, he suddenly changed into a woolen flannel casual suit and a small melon-skin hat. He was usually amiable and kind to others. The reporter lived opposite him and had met him once. As for the reasons for the murder, there are various rumors, and it is difficult to understand for a while.

The Tianzhang Paper Mill Rent Lawsuit 152

Landlord Refuses to Waive Four Months' Rent

When Japanese troops invaded Shanghai during the January 28th Incident, the concession boundaries were also ravaged. The Yangshupu area became an encampment zone. The Tianzhang Paper Mill, located there, had its water source cut off. Only after the Japanese troops fully retreated did things return to normal. Consequently, the mill requested the landlord, Jardine Matheson, to waive four months' rent. Jardine Matheson refused and filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, stating that according to the lease agreement, the annual rent was 15,000 taels, payable quarterly in advance. From November of last year to this month, rent arrears had accumulated for a year, requesting the court to order payment, etc. After the trial concluded, the court ruled to waive two months' rent, with the remaining arrears to be paid by the defendant. Tianzhang, dissatisfied, hired a lawyer to appeal to the Second Branch Court, requesting a four-month rent waiver, and a 50% reduction in rent for the four months from April to July. The day before yesterday afternoon, the Second High Court opened a hearing and summoned Jardine Matheson, who also hired lawyer Chen Zhongyin to represent them. They claimed that the appellant was deliberately delaying payment, as the first rent payment, according to the lease, was due on November 1st of last year, before the outbreak of hostilities. They had been in arrears for a year, owing 15,000 taels. The original judgment waived two months, leaving 12,500 taels still owed. Since they were now requesting a four-month waiver, the dispute was only over two months' rent, while they naturally acknowledged the remaining 14,000. As they still haven't paid, the appellee now, in addition to applying for enforcement, is also appealing to terminate the lease. Judge Hu then advised both parties to reconcile outside the court. If reconciliation fails, the verdict will be announced on the afternoon of the 31st of this month.

Dismissed Chinese Constable Convicted of Fraud 154

Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Zhang Jinbao from Anhui, formerly Constable No. 2032 at the Zhabei Police Station, was dismissed for negligence. He became increasingly depraved, engaging in fraud. On the 10th of this month, he suddenly went to No. 606 Xinzha Road to visit his friend Su Jinrong, falsely claiming that the General Police Station wanted to hire a shop clerk, and he could recommend him, but it would require a 50 yuan "activity fee." Su, currently unemployed, was overjoyed and willing to spend 50 yuan to obtain this job. However, he insisted on paying the money after the job was secured. Zhang then accompanied Su to the General Police Station, telling Su to wait outside while he confidently entered. He quickly returned, saying the matter had been settled and he would take him to the Gordon Road Police Station to collect his uniform. Upon arriving there, he again told Su to wait outside while he went inside alone. He then emerged and told Su that the interpreter Pan, who was in charge of uniforms, was not present. He suggested that Su hand over the 50 yuan, which could be collected later. Su refused, leading to a verbal dispute. Zhang then angrily hired a rickshaw and sped away. He went directly to Su's home, but Su had not yet returned. He feigned to Su's wife that her husband's matter had been settled. Su's wife, unaware of the deception, thanked him profusely. Zhang seized the opportunity to invite Su's wife to eat at the Shenfangzhai noodle shop near Chibang Bridge. While there, he boasted about his efforts and, without waiting for Su's wife's permission, ordered cigarettes and other items from the waiter, claiming they were gifts. He then took the items and left. The noodle shop later demanded over ten yuan from Su's wife for the meal and advance payments for goods. Because Su's wife had no money to pay, they suspected a scam and reported it to the police, who detained Su's wife and fined her ten yuan. Zhang, emboldened, went to Yuan Genlin's house at No. 203 An'nan Road on the 14th, intending to repeat the scam. However, Yuan was alert and immediately saw through his deception. He reported it to the police, who dispatched detectives and apprehended Zhang. The day before yesterday, he was sent to the First Special District Court, where Judge Wu Zhen presided over the interrogation. Police lawyer Qian Xunjiu requested a severe sentence for the defendant's repeated fraud. As a result, Judge Wu sentenced him to six months imprisonment as a warning.

Fellow Chongming Provincials in Shanghai 159

Discuss Aftermath of Da Yun Steamer Tragedy

The Da Yun Steamer, which travels between Chongming and Shanghai, recently capsized near Baozhen port. More than eighty passengers were killed. Five or sixty bodies have been recovered, but dozens are still missing. Fellow Chongming natives in Shanghai Song An, Guo Weiran, Tang Hanlin, Huang Linku, Guo Ping, Sheng Siding, Zhou Dingchang, and more than ten others met on the 21st at the Jin Chong Association on Shantou Road to discuss providing relief to the families of the victims and dealing with the aftermath. The following resolutions were made: 1. Raise funds to provide relief to the families of the victims. 2. Publicly appoint representatives Song An, Guo Ping, and Sheng Siding to go to Chongming to investigate the facts and urge the county government to severely punish the ship's crew and the manager responsible. 3. Publicly appoint members with legal expertise Guo Weiran, Gong Yiren, Song An, Guo Ping, and Huang Linyou to handle the registration of victims' families, relief efforts, and legal matters. 4. Telegraph the Central Party Headquarters, the Provincial Government, and other agencies, requesting orders to severely punish those responsible and the company officials. The text of the association's telegram is as follows: [To the Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, the Ministry of Communications, the Ministry of Interior, the Zhenjiang Provincial Government, the Department of Civil Affairs, the Department of Construction, the Department of Industry, the Department of Finance, and the High Court]: The Shanghai Yongyu Shipping Company's Chongming route Da Yun Steamer capsized near Baozhen port on its way from Chongming to Shanghai on October 13th, killing more than eighty people and causing losses of over 200,000 yuan. The cause of the accident was the crew's negligence and the company's monopoly for profit. The ship was carrying more than 600 packages of calico, which were piled on the upper deck, while the lower deck was empty, causing an imbalance. The sinking of the ship was avoidable. The calico was originally purchased by the Datong Yarn Factory in Shangsha and transported by small vehicles. The Da Yun Steamer's manager, seeking to seize this profit, changed the mode of transport to the steamer. There are two major steamers, Da Yun and Tianci, operating in the area. Tianci is in competition with Da Yun. The manager controlled the factory's steamers and did not allow Tianci to transport the goods. The 600 packages were loaded in one day. Otherwise, they would have been divided with Tianci, and only 300 packages would have been loaded, preventing the tragedy. Weiran and others believe that the company bears significant legal responsibility. Heavy cargo is usually loaded on the lower deck. Loading it on the upper deck, causing an imbalance, clearly foreshadowed the capsize. Maritime transport is most vulnerable to wind and rain. The ship's officers only sought profit and failed to avoid danger, leading to the tragedy. Their actions are reprehensible and deserve punishment. Weiran and others have been publicly appointed to oversee relief efforts and the aftermath, fulfilling our hometown duties. We hereby provide the cause of the accident and request your esteemed offices to send personnel to thoroughly investigate and order Chongming County Magistrate Shen Jiang to immediately arrest those responsible and the company officials for severe punishment. We are eternally grateful.

Publication of "Illustrated History of the Songhu Anti-Japanese Bloody Battle" 161

The Songhu Anti-Japanese Battle of the 19th Route Army and the 5th Army shook the world. Recognizing the greatness of this war, the Shanghai Wenhua Fine Arts and Book Company collected materials from various military departments, agencies, and individuals involved in the battle to compile the "Illustrated History of the Songhu Anti-Japanese Bloody Battle" to preserve it for posterity. Since the launch of the pre-sale, domestic and foreign subscribers have been very enthusiastic. The book has now been published. The editors are Liang Xueqing and Xu Guozhen. The size is over fifteen inches in length and eleven inches in width, making it the largest Chinese publication. The content includes over 47 three-color and two-color illustrations, over ten color and monochrome wartime battle formations, and approximately one thousand monochrome copperplate illustrations, along with over 170,000 words of text. It is magnificent, beautiful, and accurately represents the greatness of the war without omission. The actual selling price is six yuan silver dollars. Subscribers in Shanghai can pick up the book at the company's distribution point at Qipan Street Wumalu. Those outside Shanghai will receive their books on the 26th. After the book has been delivered to subscribers, only a few copies will remain. Those who want to purchase it should do so quickly.

I only go to the attached factory's Song handover office every day to handle the closing and inventory matters that were handled by former director Song during his tenure. But I have absolutely no right to interfere in any affairs of the factory after October 1st. The report is entirely untrue. Please correct it immediately to avoid confusion and clarify the truth. Sincerely, Lin Tongxing, October 23rd.

Section VII: Supplementary Matters 177

Chapter 1: Reforms to the Proposed Board of Directors' Procedures and the Development of the Committee System

1. In the fifth section of this report, there is a recommendation regarding various reform plans, which states that the Board of Directors should be expanded, with a minimum of twenty-two directors and a maximum of no more than thirty. (Note 1) If this recommendation is implemented, I believe that the Board's procedures should be revised in certain aspects to adopt a procedure that is more suitable for the needs of a larger group. However, even if there is no increase in the number of directors, there are aspects of the current procedures that should be reformed, which I would like to propose for consideration.

2. By "procedures," I do not only mean the practical methods used by the Board of Directors to handle affairs during meetings. I use this term to encompass the methods used by the Board to make decisions and to put those decisions into effect. In other words, the various methods used by the Board to keep its affairs well-organized and to fulfill all the responsibilities of a body responsible for governing the Public Concession, and to control a large-scale administrative organization, which is composed of various departments directed by key personnel to handle municipal affairs, and which can be used to achieve administrative goals.

3. The Board of Directors currently has fourteen directors, nine foreign and five Chinese. According to the Land Regulations passed in 1869, the number of directors should be "no more than nine and no fewer than five" (Article 10), and "three directors present shall constitute a quorum" (Article 22). However, due to the addition of three Chinese directors, which was passed by the Ratepayers' Meeting in 1926 and first implemented in April 1928, the number of directors increased to twelve. In May 1930, another proposal was passed, approving the addition of two more Chinese directors, bringing the total number of directors to fourteen, which is the current number. Although Article 22 of the Land Regulations, which states that a quorum is met with three directors present, has not been repealed, the current rules of the Board of Directors stipulate that a quorum is met with nine directors present. (Note 2)

4. It is important to remember that the Board's current procedures were developed through experience to meet the needs of a group that, for most of its history, never exceeded nine members. The procedures usually followed by the Board meetings can be described as the informal procedures of a small executive body, the advantage of which lies in its freedom and simplicity. If circumstances are favorable, it can handle a large amount of business in a short period with the simplest of procedures. However, it is quite obvious that the methods currently followed, apart from any other criticisms that may be raised, are probably inadequate to meet the needs of a group composed of twenty or more people, because if one seeks a reasonable economy of time while wanting to give each director ample opportunity to express his views, then the debates of more than twenty directors must inevitably take on a more formal nature.

A. Benefits of the Committee System

5. I believe there is a fairly reliable rule: the larger the administrative body, the more it must be prepared to delegate its work to committees in order to maintain its efficiency. Smaller committees can thoroughly study the details of various issues, and can make final decisions on less important issues. When there are various issues for which it is not authorized to make a final decision, it can prepare detailed reports, along with specific recommendations on how to handle them, and submit them to the larger, aforementioned administrative body.

This rule is especially applicable to a body such as the Board of Directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council, because in addition to the ordinary administrative problems involved in supervising a large organization, the Board often faces various difficult policy issues, and therefore cannot dedicate most of its time to paying attention to the detailed situations of the various offices.

6. Regarding any reforms to the proposed procedures of the Board of Directors, I believe that the main issue to be considered is the committee system. This issue involves considering the following points: (1) How should the Board's work be distributed among the various committees? What should be the limits of the power delegated to each committee? (2) What should be the relationship between the various committees and the heads of the various departments? (3) What should be the procedures and nature of the reports submitted by the committees to the Board? What procedures should be followed when the Board meetings discuss the reports of the committees?

7. The fifth section of this report mentioned the extent to which the committee system is currently used in handling the affairs of the Board of Directors (Note 3), and made several recommendations regarding certain reforms that seem appropriate. (Note 4)

8. In the sections mentioned above, it was stated that "the full benefits of the committee system cannot be obtained under the current system." (Note 5) It would be very convenient to briefly consider the main benefits that can be expected from the full development of the committee system, and the current limitations on enjoying these benefits.

9. The committee system, as usually applied to municipal government work, means that all the work of the city council is undertaken by its council members in groups, with each group being a committee. This arrangement allows for full supervision and control over the administration of the various parts of the city government, while also allowing a large portion of the trivial matters, which can be well managed by a smaller committee, to be handled without the need for the entire city council to handle them.

10. If the committee system is implemented effectively, its main benefits can be summarized as follows:

(1) Division of Labor: This approach saves the time of the entire Board of Directors, while enabling the Board to maintain full supervision and control over its administrative agencies through the various committees. As committee members often consult with each other and with the heads of the relevant departments, they gain special opportunities to become familiar with the affairs of the Municipal Council in the areas they oversee.

(2) Speedy Handling: Matters that the committees have the authority to make final decisions on can be implemented immediately without waiting for the Board's approval. (3) All important matters, most notably issues regarding large expenditures or general policies, can receive more complete and thorough consideration after being initially reviewed by the committee before being submitted to the Board. Therefore, matters that require the Board's decision are considered at least twice before a final decision is made - first by the committee and then by the Board. The regular convening of the Board to address the issues raised in the committee reports provides a valuable safeguard for the Board's decisions, avoiding the danger of decisions being based on insufficient facts, or without thorough consideration, or with unclear wording. And the committee's report can be prepared in such a way as to focus the Board's attention on matters of principle, without spending too much time discussing unimportant details.

11. Under normal circumstances, there is an important distinction between the discussions of a committee and the discussions of the Board of Directors: committee meetings are not open to the public, while Board meetings are open to the public, and the proceedings of the meetings are published in the newspapers. However, there is no such distinction in Shanghai. Because of special circumstances in Shanghai, although short formal reports of the proceedings of both the Board meetings and the committee meetings are published by the newspapers, the meetings are not open to the public. (Note 6) (To be continued)

Finance 179

Gold Market Advances Lightly Last Week

Last week, the trend of gold futures was steady, gradually rising, advancing daily without turning back, but without excessive volatility, with daily differences of only three or four taels. Initially, the silver market was nearing backwardation, and U.S. silver also fell, so the opening was high at 728.8 taels. However, the lowest price of the day was 727.4 taels. Afterwards, it frequently rose, already breaking through 30 taels. However, the overseas silver market saw little change, so the price of gold was also slightly volatile. The exchange rate suddenly plummeted, causing the local exchange market to deviate. Sterling and the U.S. dollar rose, with traders closing positions far from the market, tending towards selling. By Friday, it suddenly broke out of its silence, again showing a lively scene, as the Cantonese banks Hengxing and Yifeng fiercely resisted short positions. Various short sellers also rushed to buy, pushing both sides to close U.S. dollar positions, and the price of gold abruptly broke through the 40-tael mark. However, with profitable arbitrage opportunities available, and many taking the opportunity to sell, and with banks willing to sell, and the exchange rate rising again, and bills of exchange not being too tight, the extent of the gold price rise was not rapid. Although the silver market fell on the weekend, it was unaffected. The morning was flat, but later Hengxing added purchases, and others followed suit, reaching a high price of 745.1 taels (a weekly increase of 17.6 taels), with a high-low difference of 17.7 taels. As a result, the 44.2 taels continued to rise 17.6 taels compared to the previous Saturday (the difference between the opening and closing prices was an increase of 15.4 taels). There were still quite a few of the November contracts that had not been closed. At the beginning of the week, it had been done at (long positions paying) within 3 taels, but later it was raised to 5.75 taels, because short positions were quickly being closed, and long positions were increasing because of a shortage of cash loans, hence the increase. The volume of December contracts was estimated to be only within 20,000. The Cantonese bank Hengxing has shifted from short to long, now approximately 6,000 more long positions. Overseas silver prices were flat for sterling and falling for U.S. silver. The exchange rate fell by 4.5 points for sterling against the U.S. dollar, and by 4.625 points for the U.S. dollar against sterling, a decline for six consecutive weeks. Chinese gold trading firms initially took short positions and then covered, with the arbitrage price initially far and then approaching, so there was covering and resale of gold futures. Securities 181

Bond Prices Continued to Rise by 0.3-0.4 Last Week

| Total Turnover of 19 Million Yuan in the Whole Week |

During the past week (from October 17th to 22nd), the market conditions for various bonds on the Shanghai Chinese Stock Exchange and futures were generally very weak in the first half of the week. The sentiment among buyers and sellers was extremely sluggish, and the benefits were significantly less than in the previous week. The turnover was only over 1.6 million on Monday and only 1.8-1.9 million on Tuesday and Wednesday. However, in the second half of the week, the prices gradually increased, and the futures trading became more active, which caused the market to suddenly become more lively and the turnover to increase significantly. The turnover was 3.7 million on Friday, and approximately 5 million each on Thursday and Saturday. The total turnover for the entire week was 19,005,000 yuan, which was an increase of 6.5 million yuan compared to the previous week. Among them, the unified salt tax, 20 Customs, Disbandment and other bonds performed better than before. The October contracts for the salt tax were 2.15 million, and the November contracts were 2,135,000 yuan. The October contracts for the unified tax were 1.65 million, and the November contracts were 1.63 million yuan. The October contracts for the Disbandment bonds were 1.19 million, and the November contracts were 1.2 million yuan. The October contracts for the 20 Customs bonds were 1.47 million, and the November contracts were 985,000 yuan. The October contracts for the 20 Customs bonds were 1,335,000 yuan, and the November contracts were 760,000 yuan. The October contracts for the 19 Customs bonds were 1.01 million, and the November contracts were 485,000 yuan. The October contracts for the 19 Benevolence bonds were 970,000, and the November contracts were 390,000. The October contracts for the Reorganization bonds were 680,000, and the November contracts were 415,000 yuan. However, other bonds were still very weak. The total turnover for customs duties was 340,000, Reorganization 6% 150,000, 96 Public Bonds 60,000 yuan, and no trading for Financial bonds. Although various bonds had spot market openings, the turnover continued to be sparse, with a total turnover of only 33,000 yuan for the entire week. As for the price changes of various bonds during the past week, the market environment was still calm and unchanged due to the depressed domestic and international situations and the lack of new developments compared to before. Therefore, the price trends of various bonds were still very peaceful, with no major fluctuations and remaining in a hovering state throughout the week. As the end of the month approached and the settlement period was getting closer, the futures trading increased, and the retail investors in the market were quite active in covering their positions, so the prices generally trended upward. According to the changes, the prices were slightly lower by about 0.2 on Monday, and increased by about 0.2 per day between Tuesday and Wednesday. The upward trend was slightly stronger on Thursday and Friday, with an increase of about 0.3-0.5 per day. However, on the last day of the week, more bonds were sold out, and the prices declined slightly. As a result, the prices were higher by about 0.4-0.5 compared to the previous week, but the spot loan for customs duties in October, the spot loan for 19 Benevolence bonds, and the November contract loans each increased by more than 1 yuan. Considering the situation of the bond market, it is still depressed, and as the settlement period is approaching, the current month will soon be closed. It is difficult to expect development for the future for the time being. Yarn and Cotton 182

The Yarn Market Was Slightly Tighter Last Week

Cotton yarn trended slightly steady during the past week. After a sharp decline in market prices, a portion of profit-takers covered their positions, causing the market to rise slightly. Some of the long positions of the Wing On factory are , most closed their positions and moved from near to far contracts, showing that they were unwilling to abandon their bullish outlook. At the same time, prices were already low, and new sellers were wary. There was a relative shortage of chips in the market, so the market showed a tight situation. However, the short positions of Shenxin and Shao’s were still being released and not covered, and the fighting in Sichuan and Shandong had not yet settled, so the sentiment was still bearish, and both sides were still releasing positions. There was considerable opposition from both sides, and the prospects were uncertain. Among the foreign buyers, Shiru was more active than in the previous week, and most of the purchases were still made by the Nanbu and Chaoshan buyers. Although the fighting in Sichuan had not yet stopped, business was more active than before on the weekend. The total volume for the week was 8,685 bales, an increase of 6,719 bales compared to the previous week, and prices rose by approximately 2 taels. However, the price of Zhongsha yarn, 20s count from the Shenxin factory, was uniquely cheap in the market. The volume of yarn futures traded was 128,450 bales. Cotton Market Under High Pressure Last Week 183

The cotton market has been sluggish all week, as the overseas US and Indian cotton markets have trended downward, and the domestic Zhengxin cotton is entering the market, resulting in a bearish sentiment. Some manufacturers have sold short positions of over 200,000 piculs, and the pressure is very strong. Currently, yarn sales are sluggish and financing is extremely tight, and most people in the business community are tending toward short positions. However, although the environment is extremely bad, farmers are holding back from selling because prices are already low, so although the new cotton is on the market, the sources from various regions have not been enthusiastic. As for a certain manufacturer’s aggressive sale of approximately 50,000 piculs in October alone, now that the delivery period is approaching, there is not enough cash cotton for a very large delivery in time. The Cotton Inspection Bureau has already sampled and inspected approximately 20,000 piculs of cash cotton, and still lacks half of it. On Saturday, the Exchange again convened a council to study the delivery issue, and the details are unknown, so the standard cotton for October may still change on Monday. Judging from the overall situation of the cotton market, it will not break away from the flat and sluggish situation, but the short positions sold out are too large. The total volume of cotton futures traded in a week was 352,200 piculs. The sources on the docks included 14,203 bales of Yao cotton and 4,146 bales of Tong cotton. Grains: Rice Market Small, Moderate, and Stable 185

Shanghai South: Yesterday, arrivals were slightly fewer, and trading in the local market remained sluggish. New arrivals from Changshu and Xixi opened at a reduced price of 0.20 yuan. Kiln-grown Baige rice was sold as soon as it arrived, with no price fluctuations. Rice from Suzhou, Wujiang, and Tongli was scarce, with little to no market. Daily transactions totaled approximately 700 to 800 piculs.

New Zhabei: Yesterday, over 30 boats arrived from various inland regions. Trading in the market was active in the morning but slowed down in the afternoon. Old, inferior rice was sold off at nearly a foot below market price. Kiln-grown rice was sold at break-even prices, with no price changes. There were few buyers for wharf-stored Jian rice, indicating a downstream trend.

Northern and Southern Goods: Wood Market Continues to Tighten 186

Recently, due to scarce arrivals, the wood market continues to tighten. Previously, Sichuan fungus arrivals had opened at 51 taels, but are now being quoted at 54 taels without any transactions. News from Hankou indicates that premium Shi fungus has risen to 43.6 taels, requiring nearly 53 taels for Shanghai delivery. However, trading in Shanghai is not particularly active, making it difficult to raise prices excessively. Yesterday, high-quality local brands of fungus were offered at 53-54 taels, while Shi fungus was sold at over 49 taels, now at 50 taels. Further price increases will depend on increased sales.

Silk and Tea: Silk Market Sales Weak Last Week 187

European and American demand is lacking; Japanese silk sales remain relentless.

Last week, the Shanghai foreign firm silk market continued to experience sluggish sales. The New York market remained competitive with Japanese silk. Previously, Japanese silk's inferior quality required blending with Chinese silk for weaving. Now, Japanese silk merchants are improving their reeling techniques, selecting Japanese silk with higher tensile strength for export to New York. As a result, Japanese silk exports to the U.S. are increasing, and demand for Chinese silk is declining. Currently, there are 4,000 to 5,000 bales of yellow, white, Jing, and Guangdong gray Jing silk in stock, sufficient to meet demand for over a month. Telegrams from New York to Shanghai were infrequent and prices remained low. In Lyon, winter silk orders were weak and actual sales were stagnant. In England, there were only spot transactions. Overall, there was no turnaround in spot silk sales last week. Only American and French firms replenished their inventories, with little new development. Spot silk transactions totaled less than 300 bales, while exports totaled over 400 bales. European and American Chinese silk prices appeared stable but were implicitly weakening due to exchange rate fluctuations. Textiles: Medium-Thick Serge Plummets in Price by Several Coins 188

The medium-thick serge market has weakened recently, with public sales plummeting by several coins. For example, Tianyou's No. 1000 and No. 2000 serge were sold last week at 4.10 taels per yard, but are now being sold at 3.85 taels. Genuine old brands are priced at 4.30-4.40 taels (compared to 4.75 taels last week). The reason for the price drop is large inventories and sluggish sales. The market for medium-thick serge relies entirely on Western clothing tailors, who have already placed their orders. Sales in the local market have slowed due to the influence of new-style Hanling Peng wool and the colder weather, causing holders of goods to panic and sell off at reduced prices.

Yunzhu Wool Fails to Sell 189

In the wool market, recent cold weather has unexpectedly stimulated sales, particularly for thick wool materials used for various overcoats. Yuntou wool and Zhutou wool are necessary materials for both Chinese and Western-style overcoats. They were popular in Shanghai three to four years ago, but have gradually declined in popularity and are now nearly neglected. Except for minor interest from outports, there is virtually no business. As a result, prices are very low, with ordinary brands of Zhutou wool being offered at only 2.50-2.60 taels per yard. Yuntou wool is mostly out of stock, and arrivals of Zhutou wool are also scarce. The current market is dominated by old stock and Ke Xian goods from abroad.

Metals: Bamboo-Joint Steel Market Sees Turnaround 190

The bamboo-joint steel market has been characterized by abundant arrivals and uncertain sales, creating an impression of strength on the outside but weakness on the inside. The recent sales by foreign firms have further weakened the market and softened prices. The lowest prices are estimated at 63.5 taels per ton. In the past few days, the market has become slightly more active, and prices are showing an upward trend, estimated at 65 taels per ton. For specific sizes such as 3/8, 7/8, and 1 inch, a price of 70 taels at customs is necessary to secure supply. The reason for the price increase is twofold: high set prices and strong purchasing by speculators, and the high costs of previous orders by traders, resulting in significant losses. As a result, traders are hesitant to place new orders, leading to reduced arrivals. The market atmosphere has improved, boosting confidence and driving prices upward. According to insiders, if the construction industry in Shanghai picks up, the market outlook will improve further.

Free Talk

A Little Bit of Everything

Four-Character Classes of the Petty Person's Success 191

— Zhan Lu

Someone once said that there are four characters symbolizing the stages of love: first, "比" (bǐ, to compare), representing the mutual inclination of the man and woman, inseparable; second, "臼" (jiù, mortar), representing the intimate embrace of the man and woman, face to face, hand in hand; third, "白" (bái, white), signifying integration, the practice of cohabitation; fourth, "北" (běi, north), representing disagreement, moving in opposite directions, with no possibility of cooperation.

I say: There are also four characters symbolizing the success of a petty person: explained as follows:

First, "傘" (sǎn, umbrella), four petty people and one ten, all under the protection of a superior; the ten is like a plus sign, resembling A+, or B+, indicating above A, above B, implying that one superior can protect more than four petty people.

Second, "价" (jià, price), the petty person on the right wants to climb as high as the superior on the left, but falls short, so the petty person is supported by two stilts.

Third, "从" (cóng, from), the petty person has climbed to stand shoulder to shoulder with the superior, indistinguishable in rank.

Fourth, "仌" (bīng, ice), the petty person has progressed and climbed above the superior.

To know the four stages of the petty person's success, just look at the four characters symbolizing it: 傘, 价, 从, 仌. [Note: 从 is the same as 從, and 仌 is the same as 冰.]

Waterfall 192

— Jiang Ping

[Chinese people, listen!]

I remember that after the September 18th Incident last year, a scholar of world ethnicity said the following:

[There is currently a large "wet cloth" (referring to the Northeast provinces). The Germans are planning how to utilize its water power, how to irrigate fields. The British are silently going there to realize the German ideas. The Japanese, however, shouted loudly, "This is our lifeline!" and frantically ran over to seize it, claiming it as their own. As for the Chinese, the owners of this waterfall, they didn't really have any use for it, only appreciating nature and using it as material for writing poetry. So, they didn't care much about the ownership, because even if it changed owners, they could still appreciate it, still write poetry.]

At the time, I was naturally very angry after reading it. But, calmly recalling history, I couldn't find any evidence to refute it.

That was still a year ago.

Please look at the present situation: lost territory has not been recovered, national difficulties are increasingly urgent, and the people are living in a drunken stupor. Everything is still in an extremely dangerous and pathetic state! Not only that, the aggressive ambitions and encroaching steps of the powerful enemy are becoming clearer day by day. To be honest, when the lost territory in the Northeast has not been recovered and the blood of the Shanghai war is still fresh, we cannot actively serve on the battlefield and kill the enemy outside the border. We cannot destroy our homes to relieve the national crisis and provide material assistance to the brave men of the Northeast. We are already ashamed to death! We can only intensify the boycott movement in a passive way to achieve a slight effect.

Writing this, my heart is extremely heavy! I don't want to say anything more. I just want everyone to reflect: What else can you do but let people slaughter you, if you are so useless, unpromising, unconscionable, and unconscious?

The Beauty of Heroism 193

— Ji Xiang

Beauty is the source of life, a cup of fine wine in the desert, a beacon in the night, a guide in life. Without beauty, the world would die, and humans would be just a group of animals.

Does beauty have limits? The limits of beauty are truth and goodness. If it is not good, it is not beautiful. Similarly, as long as it is true and good, it is beautiful. The fiery sunrise is beautiful, the watery moonlight is beautiful, the turbulent Yangtze River is beautiful, the gentle stream is beautiful; the blood of martyrs is beautiful, the rouge of beautiful women is beautiful; the thrilling sound of guns and cannons is the beauty of heroism, and the melodious singing of women is the beauty of gentleness; solemnity is beautiful, and decadence is also beautiful. As long as it is true and good, it is beautiful. Quietness is beautiful, and especially, violence is beautiful!

At present, the world is full of the color of love. Volcanoes are erupting, the earth is shaking, rivers are boiling, and the sea is roaring. Guns and cannons have already begun to bombard us from all directions, and knives are already on our heads! All we see is hot blood, red fire, and our noses are filled with the smell of gunpowder and fishiness! The goddess of peace has gone far away! Friends, the time is getting more and more urgent, not allowing you to hesitate, not allowing you to be lazy. Which direction should you go in now? Do you still want to drink a cup of cool chrysanthemum tea? Or do you want to drink a cup of strong sorghum liquor?

It seems that someone once said that beauty requires rhythm and harmony. A cup of fragrant tea requires gentle and elegant sipping. If a rough man comes along, picks up the cup, and gulps down three big swigs, then there is no rhythm, no harmony is lost, and what lacks harmony and rhythm cannot be considered beautiful. Indeed, beauty requires rhythm and harmony. However, is harmony and rhythm only found in gentle expressions? General Fan sat down and cut pork to eat, how vulgar! However, that is still the greatest beauty in the world! Similarly, Emperor Gaozu of Han's "Song of the Great Wind" is rough and simple, but is still recited to this day. Saying that a cup of fine tea must be sipped slowly to be considered beautiful is something only Lin Daiyu and Jia Baoyu in "Dream of the Red Chamber" would do. I don't say that, I just love to gulp down three big swigs.

The reality is that we no longer have the opportunity to slowly savor that cup of fragrant tea! The pure talk of the Wei and Jin dynasties was enough to ruin the country! Friends, now we must learn from the brave men of ancient Sparta, fighting alone, dominating the world, and living that extraordinary, rough life! We must immediately abandon gentle enjoyment, shallow pursuits, low-level material desires, and a relaxed and lazy peaceful life. We must tighten the blood vessels throughout our bodies and plunge into the flames! We must put down the fragrant and soft rice and bite into the dark and hard cornbread! From now on, we must no longer be fascinated by the gentle melodies, but learn from the ancient Qin people's hitting the pottery and calling out "wu wu," and sing our heroic battle songs! We must have the heat of the sun and the surge of the Yangtze River! Only burning like fire is our only way out from now on! Friends, rise up! Rise up and open up our world of heroic beauty!

The Buying and Selling System and Speculative Nature 194

— Meng Lan

[Such is Marriage]

Everything is progressing; marriage, a major life event, has also progressed from a buying and selling system to a speculative nature. In the past, parents sold their children as [machines for producing people], regardless of the consent of the parties involved, relying only on their own likes and dislikes. The seller only wanted to sell at a good price and then [would deny the debt], regardless of whether the daughter was treated well, abandoned, or abused, as if she were not their daughter at all. They would then say with feigned sympathy, [Alas! My daughter has such a thin life]. Otherwise, [a daughter who has been married off is like water that has been poured out], living is as part of the X family, dying is as a ghost of the X family.

The buyer only wanted the machine to be able to produce people, not caring about anything else, except for haggling over the price; as for whether they could [be happily married forever], that depended on the child's good fortune!

Now it seems to be progressing. The buying and selling marriages under the so-called old etiquette have been fundamentally shaken and shattered. The young masters and young ladies put on the iron helmet of [free love] and proceed in all directions.

But the so-called [free love] is simple enough that you can't believe it. After a trip to the park! Of course, it doesn't have to be a park! After a few conversations, they start to [regret not meeting sooner]. A week later, they start entering and exiting the doors of hotels together. When the melon is ripe and the stem falls off, they have to invite two [supporting actors] to play a comedy once. What happens after marriage? That depends on whether HEBE is always by her side, and whether he is followed by the God of Wealth.

Everything is progressing; marriage, a [major life event], has also progressed from a buying and selling system to a speculative nature.

Note: HEBE is the goddess of youth.

Brief News: The acupuncture physician, Mr. Fang Shen'an, has long been known for his miraculous needles. Because patients often regard needles with fear, he has deeply researched the ancient moxibustion method of our country and invented various electrotherapy devices. Mr. Fang believes that the electrotherapy of Western medicine sometimes corresponds to the principles of our country's moxibustion method. However, moxibustion scorches the skin, causing pain to the patient. Western medicine uses electrical heat without any medicine. If they can be integrated and applied, the effect will be significant. Last year, Mr. Fang's medicated electrotherapy achieved great results. The method involves using electricity to transmit heat and penetrate medicinal vapors into the skin. Since its application, the effect has been miraculous. Now, he has gone a step further and created electric acupuncture, which uses the power of electrical heat to directly reach the meridians through the needle tips, penetrating deep into the interior, with unexpectedly great effects. (Yi)

In addition, the brothers Shanzi and Daqian Zhang, of the Dafeng Hall, have been collecting calligraphy and paintings from the Tang, Song, Yuan, Ming, and Qing dynasties for twenty years, which are rich and exquisite. They will be selected and exhibited at the Art Appreciation Society, No. 80 Hualong Road, from the 27th to the 31st of this month. Some of them will be available for transfer if there are appreciators, in order to broaden circulation. (Zizai)

Tune: Washing Brook Sand 195

— Qian Xiaoshan

The painted horn blows until the end, but does not stop. I cannot bear the barbarian fighting like mayflies. How many times have I tethered my horse and gazed at the divine land.

Sunset is hard to gather, chrysanthemums drip tears. Scattered clouds are all given to the sorrows of broken geese. The scenery of the rivers and mountains again startles the autumn.

Entering the Pass Post Companions (20) 196

— Seeking Happiness Studio Master

Lu Boqin was very distressed when he received the news about the postal bureau being in danger. Because even if he could safely leave the country, he would be forced to abandon his lover and go far away! The postal rights of the Republic of China in the Northeast would be lost at the same time as his lover, which was truly extremely unfortunate, and he couldn't help but be distressed. But the reality was difficult to reverse, and he definitely couldn't abandon his lover. Could he stay here alone? He had already felt that his actions were not very free these past few days, and it often seemed like a little ghost detective was watching him closely from behind. If he didn't surrender to the Japanese and willingly continue to work in the postal bureau of Manchukuo, would the Japanese let him stay here for no reason? Surrender! This was something he would rather die than do. Staying here without leaving, even if he wasn't afraid of death, he still couldn't live without money. After thinking it over, he really had no solution! So, he became anxious and thought about joining the Volunteer Army nearby. He would be able to face the country, and he wouldn't be too far from his lover. However, he still couldn't find a way to join the Volunteer Army, it was just a pipe dream.

During this period of ants climbing on a hot pot, he still met with Tong Yizhen many times in the open air, and they sighed in vain, but still couldn't find a good solution. However, he received strange news from Tong Yizhen that Tong Guifu had suddenly become active on his own these days, and was happily active outside; and even some sneaky Japanese people came to Tong's house, talking secretly behind closed doors, not letting Yizhen hear. He couldn't guess what wonderful medicine this uncle of his, a citizen of Manchukuo, was hiding in his gourd?

One day at dusk, Tong Yizhen suddenly grabbed Lu Boqin at the entrance of the alley and reported in a panic:

[Didn't you tell me to pay more attention to my uncle's recent strange behavior? This matter has finally been revealed today! As expected, it is very related to me. My uncle has joined the Concordia Party and has been instructed by the Japanese to organize a delegation of young girls from Manchuria to visit Japan. These young girls are not easy to find, so he recommended me! That's why the Japanese came to my house to examine my appearance. Today, the Japanese have recognized me as qualified, and came to inform me in person, and said that after returning from Japan, we young girls who have been on a mission will be treated generously and transferred to the Changchun Executive Government to become imperial consorts. The reason is that the Japanese do not agree with Emperor Puyi's recent plan to re-employ eunuchs from the old imperial palace in Beijing, so they proposed to replace them with a batch of imperial consorts. Ten young girls each will be selected from Japan, Korea, and Manchuria to fill the vacancies for imperial consorts. I was unfortunately selected by them again! When I heard this, I originally couldn't agree; but you advised me not to directly conflict with them, so I just politely declined for a while. I specifically came to you to think of a solution. But I have long known that you are indecisive. If you continue to hesitate, you will enter the pass, and I will go to Japan and then to that Executive Government in Changchun to become an imperial consort. We will be separated forever, with no hope of reunion!

Shanghai Local Supplement to Shen Bao

Opinion

Teacher Liu's Demagoguery Confounds the Masses 197

— Buddha

Emperor Gaozu of Han did not slay the white snake to gain the world. He did not invite Zhang Zifang, who traveled with Chisongzi, to become his prime minister. He did not, like Liu Xuan'de taking Sichuan, invite Zhuge Liang, who wore a Bagua robe, held a white feather fan, and could borrow the east wind but not the west wind, to become his strategist. He did not, like Song Jiang and the thirty-six Heavenly Spirits and seventy-two Earthly Fiends running rampant on the Water Margin, invite Ru Yunlong Gongsun Sheng, who carried an ancient Song-patterned sword on his back and recited incantations, to become his military advisor. Our country's history of creating mysterious and peculiar events with ghosts and gods is mostly like this.

Now I see reported that the cause of this Sichuan war [is because Liu Xiang believed in heresies and listened to Liu Chongyun's demagoguery. Chongyun is skilled in Daoist arts. Liu Xiang trusts him greatly, respecting him as a teacher. All military and state affairs, as well as personal conduct, are decided by the teacher. The teacher once said that Xiang is the largest star in Sichuan, and will one day dominate one side. A few days ago, Teacher Liu fasted for seven days and seven nights, bathed and dressed in incense, ascended the stage to examine the celestial phenomena, and said that he had been allowed by Heaven to appoint Yue Wumu as the commander-in-chief and Pang Shiyuan as the chief of staff. As long as forty-nine days pass, Sichuan can be unified.] Liu Xiang listened to the teacher's nonsense and created the tragic disaster of the Two Lius in Sichuan. It is not surprising that these ambitious warlords would be elated and start a war after hearing such fantastical tales.

Using gods to establish teachings is our country's old trick. However, it is somewhat unwise for Heaven to appoint two gods, Yue Wumu and Pang Shiyuan, to be the commander-in-chief and chief of staff. Yue Wumu devoted himself to serving the country and obeyed the central government's call to return to the capital, but was eventually harmed by Qin Hui and did not achieve his ambition of restoring the country. Pang Shiyuan assisted Liu Xianzhu in taking Sichuan, but died from an arrow in Luofeng Slope and did not achieve great success either. Even when these two gods were alive, they did not achieve their goals. Now that Heaven has sent two gods to be Liu Xiang's commander-in-chief and chief of staff, I am afraid that these two gods will also say [We refuse to participate in internal wars and respectfully decline].

[Demagoguery arises from people] It is also said that [When a country is about to perish, there will be demons]. The warlords do not consider their own strength or the overall situation of the country, but listen to the demagoguery and act willfully. I think there will be some danger. The Empress Dowager Cixi of the late Qing dynasty listened to the words of the Boxers and supported Qing in destroying foreigners. Guns and cannons did not enter, and as a result, the emperor had to flee and the Eight-Nation Alliance entered Beijing. The effect was that they were completely fooled. This is very recent historical material. If Teacher Liu really has the ability, he should invite the gods from the Investiture of the Gods or invite Sun Dasheng from Journey to the West, who can somersault 108,000 li in one jump.

Also, yesterday's report said that Teacher Liu went to the front line to supervise the battle, riding in a yellow sedan chair, accompanied by a teaching division and three battalions of guards. The military appearance was magnificent, and the viewers filled the road. There has been no such military honor since Tang Jiyao. This is really a monster. This is really a strange thing and very interesting.
