Respectfully Inscribing After Reading "The Words and Deeds of Yang Zhongmin Gong" 199

Vowing to exhaust my strength to eradicate traitors,

Persisting in sacrificing myself for the country with sincerity.

Spring and Autumn annals condemn the rebellious,

Blood and flesh repay my sovereign.

Having the ambition to achieve righteousness,

Having no concern for life or death.

The future will praise Cang Shui’s fire,

The past praises Xiaoru’s chastity.

His spirit is as calm as the mountains and rivers,

His radiance can match the sun and moon.

The words and deeds are clearly recorded,

The gods weep and heaven is astonished.

Science

A Method for Artificially Drying Fresh Flowers 200

— Ke Quan

The freshness and vibrancy of most flowers usually only last for a short time before they wither, which is such a pity, isn't it? Now, there is a method where we can artificially dry fresh flowers, preserving their original freshness for a long time. This is a great invention, written below:

We only need to prepare a wooden box and some white sand to pick the flowers and start drying them.

First, spread a layer of white sand on the bottom of the box, put the flowers on the sand surface, and arrange them in the desired pose. Then, gently open the petals, slowly fill the flower with white sand, and then lightly sprinkle more white sand, burying the entire flower. Cover the box.

After doing this, place the sand box in a dry and warm place, noting the date. After two weeks, gently push aside the white sand in the sand box to see if there is any moisture on the petals. If not, then you have succeeded. If the petals are not yet completely dry, they must be reburied.

We must know that ordinary fresh flowers take about two to three weeks to dry, but it depends on the climate. If the temperature is high, the flowers will dry faster; if the temperature is low, the flowers will dry slower. This is something we should pay attention to.

If the petals in the sand box are completely dry, doesn't that mean it's successful? At that time, we will slowly remove the sand! It is best if the wooden boards around the box are removable so they can be taken apart at will, allowing the sand to spread out on its own. Then, take the flowers out. If there is sand or dust on the flowers, use a wool brush (soft chicken or duck feathers are also acceptable) to gently brush it off. Be especially careful at this time, because the dried petals are very fragile.

Now, take these dried fresh flowers and place them in a vase on the desk, and they will never wither again.

Finally, I must also make it clear. The flowers that are picked must be dry and whole. Those with dew or raindrops on them cannot be used. It is easy to tell whether the flowers are contaminated with dew or raindrops. Just pay attention, and you can recognize it. However, the white sand that is taken must also be very clean. If there are any impurities inside, they cannot be used either. To make the white sand very clean, there must be another procedure: washing. Although ordinary white sand looks very white, it actually contains some dust, so it must be washed. We put the white sand in a white porcelain basin and pour clear water in, stirring the sand. Then the heavy sand sinks to the bottom, and the light dust floats to the top, turning the water cloudy. Then slowly pour out the dirty water, replace it with some clean water, and repeat this exchange

Page 16

several times until the water poured in, no matter how stirred, is no longer cloudy. Only then is the white sand considered clean. Then pour out the water, place the sand in a ventilated place to dry, and at the same time, be careful not to let dust fall into the white sand. This washed white sand can then be used with confidence.

Reform Society Discussion Group

Suggestions for Reforming the Almanac 201

— Chi Fo

Since the establishment of the Republic of China, the Ministry of Education's Central Observatory has compiled new almanacs every year and distributed them to government offices in various provinces. However, the government offices did not widely distribute them, so very few people knew about them. In recent years, the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau has also issued a new type of almanac, making great efforts to distribute it. The compilation method is good, and the price is low, but not many people buy it. On the other hand, the Guangdong almanac and small popular almanacs are outdated, crude, and popular in society. Even the most widely sold "National Quick Guide" has many shortcomings in its content. I believe that the reform of Chinese almanacs is a good opportunity to enhance national common sense and transform outdated thinking. How can it be said to be a trivial matter and neglected? Now, I will briefly list a few reasons that urgently need reform:

(1) Fostering Superstition. Try to look at the Guangdong almanac used in society. Not only is the printing poor, but it is still woodcut, truly a printing from eighty years ago. The content is extremely absurd and shallow. In addition to the lunar calendar being the main thing that urgently needs reform, there are countless paradoxical records. The people are influenced by what they see and hear every day, and their thinking becomes vulgar and their knowledge immature. The failure to improve the almanac is also a major reason. For example, the book states that the Noble Spirit is in the southeast, the God of Wealth is due north, the God of Joy is northwest, and it is auspicious to increase the population, enter school, raise the beams, travel, break ground, receive wealth, bathe, sign contracts... and so on. Everything one sees promotes superstition, doesn't it? The Heavenly Stems and Earthly Branches are originally a kind of pronoun used by the ancients to record time. Now, when people encounter major events such as weddings and funerals, they either ask blind fortune-tellers to calculate or consult date-selection shops. These date-selection wizards rely on the almanac. Therefore, this tattered almanac of dozens of pages is actually a secret manual for witches and sorcerers to deceive people! Also, the Spring Ox Picture is meaningless, and the Twenty-Eight Mansions are even compared to the twenty-eight famous generals during the reign of Emperor Guangwu of the Eastern Han Dynasty, making them the divine names of the twenty-eight constellations in the sky. Furthermore, things like "Good Luck Opening the Door on New Year's Day" and "Good Luck Burning Incense on New Year's Day" are absurd, unfounded, and written in strange and vulgar language. Shouldn't they be urgently reformed?

(2) Other Errors. The almanac only records the times of solar and lunar eclipses and the rise and fall of tides without explaining the reasons,

which is also a defect. Things like [Rotten grass turns into fireflies] and [Sparrows entering the great water turn into clams] although related to the solar terms, [have already been said in the Book of Months.] However, the theories are erroneous and do not make sense in terms of animal physiology. They are truly an obstacle to science and should be urgently deleted. In addition, the birthdays of gods and Buddhas are specially commemorated, which is also laughable. I believe that national humiliation commemorations, scientific common sense, the current situation in the three northeastern provinces, surveys of domestic and foreign goods, common sense of geography and history, records of books, arithmetic, transportation, etc., should all be added. Furthermore, common sense for businessmen, family organization, personal cultivation, and common sense for social interaction should be included to provide practical use. Alas! The popular almanacs on the market today not only increase national superstition but also greatly violate the national system. Shouldn't they be urgently reformed?

I don't have the time to refute the errors of the popular almanacs on the market, but since the authorities have clearly ordered them to be banned, why are these almanacs still selling so well everywhere? It is truly a question! The absurd almanac of the twenty-second year is about to be published again. I wonder what measures the local authorities have in place?

Cunning

The Difficulty of Reading Hearts 202

— Shi Ben

My old friend Mr. Xiong, who works in the police force, suddenly received the terrible news of his wife's death. He was filled with grief, rubbed his eyes full of tears of blood, and hurriedly asked his superiors for leave, rushing home as quickly as possible.

After sadly taking care of her funeral, he suddenly thought about what to do with the three poor motherless children she left behind. Alas! He himself, driven by life, was a sojourner in a foreign land and could not stay at home for long to raise these three children who had no ability to be independent. Alas! Since the environment did not allow him to stay at home to raise them, then he would take them with him to his post. But moving the whole family would be extremely burdensome. Moreover, those who are serving in public office now are only magistrates for a short time. Today they are here, and tomorrow they are transferred there. Wouldn't it be difficult to move back and forth? It would be better to hire an honest old woman to entrust her with the responsibility of raising them, so that he could still go out to make a living. That would be the best of both worlds. Fortunately, the eldest daughter was already thirteen years old, and the youngest was also seven years old. Neither of them needed breastfeeding. The old woman's ability could also handle it. After he decided in his heart, he hurriedly went to find an old woman near sixty years old, and handed over all the matters in the family to her management in person, and solemnly instructed her to take good care of her three sisters. After he arranged the family affairs, because the vacation was over, he had no choice but to leave his three orphaned daughters with grief and tears and return to his post.

This old woman, after entering Mr. Xiong's family, actually took on the responsibility of raising and caring for his three children as if she were their mother. The three sisters also treated her like their own mother and were very close to her. No matter what she ordered, they obeyed her completely. A week later, the three sisters, sleeping in bed at night, suddenly heard a ghostly [shh shh shh] sound outside the room, which frightened them so much that they were dumbfounded and their hearts were trembling with fear. They hurried to burrow into the quilt, covered their ears, and closed their eyes. At daybreak, the thirteen-year-old girl told the old woman about the ghost sounds at night and asked her to find a way to protect them. The old woman said, [I have heard the ghost sounds these past two nights. I sleep in the outer room and hear them every night. It almost scared me to death. Moreover, last night a small-footed female ghost came to lift my mosquito net, scaring me to hide in the quilt and tremble!] The sisters, being young and ignorant, were terrified when they heard that a ghost had come to disturb the mosquito net. They all asked the old woman to move into the same room to sleep, and at night, they asked the old woman to sew the mosquito net door with thread. While sleeping in bed, they all burrowed tightly into the quilt, completely covering their heads!

This haunting incident was known to Mr. Xiong's friend, who wrote a letter to report it to him. Mr. Xiong was very puzzled when he received the letter and immediately returned. The sisters told him about the matter, but Mr. Xiong didn't quite believe it. He was a member of the police force and was very alert. He suspected that there was something fishy about this matter, so he ran to the room to check the trunks and chests. Sure enough, as he expected, he found that more than two hundred yuan of things were missing and determined that it was the old woman's trick. He immediately detained her.

She confessed that because the three sisters were young and easily deceived, she resorted to this trick of pretending to be a ghost to scare them into submission, hiding in the quilt, and asking her to sleep in the same room, so that she could take the opportunity to steal things.

Yesterday, Mr. Xiong sent a letter to the author detailing the whole incident. After reading the original letter, I was very moved and deeply lamented the deterioration of social customs, the loss of morality, the cunning and deceitful schemes, and the difficulty of reading people's hearts. If this old woman, already in her sixties, still engages in such dishonest behavior of deception and theft, it can be seen that the current society is truly declining.

(Bulletin Board)

Shanghai Local Court 203

Criminal Judgments: Judgment on the appeal case of Gong Boda for theft (Main Text): The original judgment is revoked. Gong Boda is fined twenty-five yuan for stealing electricity, with a two-year suspended sentence. ▲ Adjudication of the case of Zhou Mao's destruction (Main Text): This case is dismissed by the plaintiff. ▲ Judgment on the case of Wang Wu Bao's injury (Main Text): Wang Wu Bao is fined twenty yuan for harming another's health. If the fine is not fully paid through forced execution, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment per yuan. ▲ Judgment on the case of Liu Yuanshun's robbery and fraud (Main Text): This public prosecution is not accepted. ▲ Judgment on the case of Pan Wei Tao's disruption of family (Main Text): Pan Wei Tao is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for inducing a twenty-year-old man to leave the person with parental rights. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Judgment on the case of Li Xiao Erzi's intimidation (Main Text): Li Xiao Erzi is sentenced to five months of imprisonment for attempted extortion through joint intimidation. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Judgment on the case of Zhang Tangsheng's theft (Main Text): Zhang Tangsheng is sentenced to ten months of imprisonment for theft. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Judgment on the case of Wang Tianqi's theft (Main Text): Wang Tianqi is sentenced to one year of imprisonment for continuous theft during a military disaster. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Judgment on the case of Lu Jinsheng's theft (Main Text): Lu Jinsheng is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for stealing property in a group of three or more. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Judgment on the case of Xin Jingliu and others' theft and obstruction of official duties (Main Text): Xin Jingliu, Xu Zhaohu, Wang Pengshou, and Zhao Hongwen are each sentenced to one year of imprisonment for jointly breaking into a residence at night to commit theft in a group of three or more. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Wang Yuchun is sentenced to three months of imprisonment for transporting stolen goods. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Liu Hongsheng is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for knowingly purchasing stolen goods. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. The remaining part of the charge of obstructing official duties is not guilty. ▲ Judgment on the case of Wang A Gen's theft (Main Text): Wang A Gen is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for breaking into a residence at night to commit theft. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Judgment on the case of Gui Yongfa and others' opium case (Main Text): Gui Yongfa is sentenced to six months of imprisonment and a fine of sixty yuan for providing a place for others to smoke opium, and is sentenced to two months of imprisonment and a fine of thirty yuan for smoking opium. The total is seven months of imprisonment and a fine of seventy yuan. If the fine is not fully paid through forced execution, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment per yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. ▲ Huang Guiwu, Xu Jingsheng, and Jin Awu are each sentenced to one month of imprisonment and a fine of thirty yuan for smoking opium. If the fine is not fully paid through forced execution, it can be converted into one day of imprisonment per yuan. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. Huang Guiwu is given a three-year suspended sentence. Two opium pipes, two lamps, two earthen pots, one opium stick, one opium scissors, seven qian of opium, fifty red pills, one opium bubble, and a small amount of opium ash are all confiscated. ▲ Judgment on the case of Tang Linsheng's theft (Main Text): Tang Linsheng is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for committing theft while carrying a weapon. The number of days of detention before the judgment is finalized will be converted into one day of imprisonment for every two days. One iron chisel is confiscated.

Civil Judgments: Ruling on the appeal case of Yang Ruikun and Pan Zhushi et al. for loan (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The costs of the third instance of the litigation are borne by the appellant. ▲ Judgment on the case of Chen Yongnian et al. and Zhengde Silver Company for rent reduction dispute (Main Text): The plaintiff's lawsuit is rejected. The litigation costs are borne equally by the plaintiffs. ▲ Judgment on the case of Wang Qingyi and Li Jiangsheng et al. for incidental civil lawsuit (Main Text): The defendants shall jointly return forty pieces of lumber to the plaintiff. The remainder of the plaintiff's lawsuit is rejected. The plaintiff bears five-sixths of the litigation costs, and the defendants jointly bear one-sixth. ▲ Judgment on the case of Jin Yiru and Qiu Ruisheng for exclusion of encroachment dispute (Main Text): The house pillars and walls built by the defendant beyond the boundary shall be immediately demolished, and the plaintiff's wall foot shall be restored to its original state. Both the plaintiff's additional lawsuit and the defendant's counterclaim are rejected. The litigation costs are borne by the plaintiff for the additional part, and the remainder is borne by the defendant. ▲ Judgment on the case of Huang Chen et al. and Old Chen Zhou et al. for estate attachment dispute (Main Text): For the fields and houses in Gaoqiao, Pudong, the fields in Nanhui County, and the houses and land on Xinzha Bridge and Datong Road, which were provisionally attached by this court on May 7 and June 10 of this year, the defendant shall be limited to one-third of the share due to Huang Shouchang, and the remaining two-thirds shall be due to the plaintiff. The defendant may not request attachment. The litigation costs are borne by the defendant. ▲ Judgment on the appeal case of Yang Ziwen and Su Yunqing for rent (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The costs of the second instance of the litigation are borne by the appellant. ▲ Judgment on the appeal case of Lu Jinsheng and You Lian Zeng for termination of agreement (Main Text): The original judgment is rescinded. The appellee's lawsuit in the first instance is rejected. The costs of the first and second instances of the litigation are borne by the appellee. ▲ Ruling on the appeal case of Gongji Transport Company and Tongda Company for loan (Main Text): The appeal is rejected. The costs of the second instance of the litigation are borne by the appellant.
